Page 4

Saarland Designated as a Demilitarized Zone, Germany Accepts in Principle

Counter-Proposal Submitted for Removal of Military Engineering

Agreement Reached on March 1st as the Return Date

Technical Issues Still to be Negotiated Between France and Germany

(Geneva) France's demand that the Saarland should be included in the demilitarized zone of the Rhineland under the Treaty of Versailles has been accepted by Germany in principle. This acceptance is contained in Germany's reply today to the draft plan of the League of Nations for the return of the Saarland. However, Germany's recent actions have not eliminated the stalemate caused by France's demand, as Germany has put forward a counter-proposal regarding the demolition of railways, barracks, and other engineering works with implicit military value in the Saarland. Another point requiring further negotiation is Germany's opposition to the proposal that if Germany and France cannot reach an agreement on technical issues by March 1st, the Council of the League of Nations should act as arbitrator. March 1st is the currently proposed date for the return of the Saarland. Consul-General Krull of Germany in Geneva discussed Germany's counter-proposal with the Committee of Three today and then telegraphed new suggestions to Berlin. The German authorities now regard France's last-minute interpretation of the demilitarization of the Saarland as the biggest obstacle to Germany's acceptance of the Geneva proposals. According to political circles in Berlin, Germany will not accept any solution that would result in the Saarland being treated differently from other demilitarized zones. (Reuters, 17th)

(Geneva) It is now known that Germany has agreed in principle to designate the Saarland as a demilitarized zone, and that Germany and France have agreed on March 1st as the date for Germany to regain sovereignty over the Saarland. Germany's reply was submitted to the French government this morning, stating that since the Treaty of Versailles has already decided the issue of the disarmament of the Saarland, there is no need to discuss the matter further. Therefore, Germany has tacitly acknowledged the Saarland as a demilitarized zone. If the French government accepts this interpretation by Germany, the Council of the League of Nations will pass a resolution on the return of the Saarland to Germany at its meeting this afternoon. (National Telegram, 17th)

(Geneva) The Saarland Committee today resolved to recommend to the Council of the League of Nations that the Saarland be returned to Germany on March 1st. However, according to reliable sources, France may demand that after the return, the Brown Shirts and Stormtroopers should still be prohibited from entering the Saarland. (National Telegram, 16th)

(Geneva) The meeting of the Council of the League of Nations, originally scheduled for 4 pm today, has now been postponed by half an hour. It is generally believed that this is a good sign and that the Saarland issue still has a chance of being resolved this month. The Chairman of the Committee of Three, Aloisi, is continuing to exchange views with the German Consul-General in Geneva, Krull, in the hope of reaching a definitive solution. German sources say that they are willing to reach an agreement, but believe that being too hasty will harm important interests. The German government has no objection to the military clauses of the Treaty of Versailles being implemented in the Saarland region, but has raised some reservations, the most important of which are the removal of military railways and the demolition of existing fortifications. The President of the Council, Turkish Foreign Minister Rüştü, hosted a luncheon for the representatives of the Council countries at noon today for a social gathering. After the banquet, French Foreign Minister Laval met with British Lord Privy Seal Eden and Italian representative Aloisi. (Havas, 17th)

(Geneva) Germany can take over the Saarland on March 1st if issues such as disarmament can be resolved first. France cited the Treaty of Versailles, demanding that all German territory on the left bank of the Rhine be demilitarized, which caused the Council of the League of Nations meeting this afternoon to fail to formally announce the return of the Saarland to Germany. European political circles were quite surprised and feared that it would cause resentment in Germany and create unnecessary complications. A compromise was drafted in the evening under the supervision of the Aloisi Committee, and people's hearts began to settle down. The solution is that before the formal return, France and Germany should negotiate existing issues, the most important of which is the demilitarization of the Saarland. If the two countries cannot reach an agreement within a week of the end of February, a special meeting of the Council of the League of Nations should be convened to resolve the dispute between the two countries. It is expected that Germany will accept this solution, and it is hoped that the Council of the League of Nations can meet tomorrow to discuss the Saarland plebiscite. It is heard that Germany has accepted in principle the extension of the demilitarized zone to the Saarland, but has not yet agreed to France's proposal to demolish certain transportation facilities related to military use. It is also heard that the Franco-German expert committee has decided to request the Council of the League of Nations to advocate the return of the Saarland to Germany between February 15th and March 1st. The Council of the League of Nations meeting this afternoon was originally intended to formally announce the return of the Saarland to Germany, but was postponed due to France's proposal for the demilitarization of the Saarland. France claimed that, according to Articles 42 to 44 of the Treaty of Versailles, no armaments or troops may be stationed on the German territory on the left bank of the Rhine, and all military railways, transportation equipment for troops and trains, and bridges and canals with military value must be demolished. The German government asked the Aloisi Committee to apply to the Council of the League of Nations to determine the date of the return of the Saarland. The French government opposed the immediate return, fearing that Germany would delay the solution of the important issue of the demilitarization of the Saarland until after the return, in which case any intervention by the League of Nations would be futile. (Reuters, 16th)

Committee of Three Redrafts Report

(Geneva) After convening a meeting for one hour this afternoon, Mr. Aloisi, Chairman of the Saarland Committee of Three, made a statement that the Committee of Three had redrafted the report to be submitted to the Council of the League of Nations. The Committee's recommendations are still based on the results of the Saarland plebiscite. The contents of the newly drafted report are not detailed, but it is known that a draft has been sent to the German Consul in Geneva for him to submit to Berlin for review by the German government. Germany will issue a statement on the report of the Committee of Three on Thursday. The Council of the League of Nations is scheduled to convene a meeting at 4 pm on Thursday, and the German government's statement will be sent to Geneva before the meeting. (National Telegram, 16th)

Customs Posts Established on the Franco-Saarland Border

Saarbrücken According to reliable sources, the French customs authorities have announced that from January 16th, a customs post should be established on the border between France and the Saarland, because according to the Treaty of Paris, the Saarland has had no customs border with France for the past fifteen years. The Saarland Mining Bureau, managed by the French, has also announced that all its staff will be dismissed at the end of February, with appropriate subsidies. After this is implemented, 1,100 French staff will be affected and will have to return to France with their families. Furthermore, the French mining bureau will also move to Metz in the near future, where suitable houses have already been rented. (National Telegram, 16th)

French Forbach The customs union between France and the Saarland has effectively been abolished. The French customs office, which was previously located on the border between the Saarland and Germany, has now been moved to the border between Lorraine and the Saarland. Some goods have been refused passage by customs on both sides. (Havas, 16th)

An Atmosphere of Revenge is Everywhere

(Paris) The special correspondents of major French newspapers stationed in Saarbrücken all say that everything in Saarbrücken is already like a German city. Anti-National Socialist Party figures have begun to withdraw from the Saarland region. "Le Matin" said, "The whole city is like it has been liberated, like the day after a holiday." "Le Journal" expressed pleasure at the peaceful order in Saarbrücken, but said, "The current situation is not yet reliable, as an atmosphere of revenge is still everywhere. Those who are strong in the German front line still want to punish those they call 'traitors' and will not give up. When Germany formally recovers the Saarland region in the future, it will inevitably carry out political retaliation. Therefore, most people, thinking of this, cannot help but feel terrified and believe that now is still a time to hide and should not miss the opportunity." Le Petit Parisien said, "The withdrawal of anti-National Socialist Party figures from the Saarland is only the beginning, but the scene in front of the French consulate is already too horrible to look at. Families who have been displaced, supporting the old and carrying the young, live in front of the consulate gate. Men and women sit on luggage baskets, and are afraid of being spied on by secret agents. They deliberately avoid showing their identity cards when they present them, and when someone takes a film, they often turn their heads to avoid being filmed." L'Echo de Paris also said that anti-National Socialist Party figures are now suffering from real fear. (Havas, 16th)

Political Exiles Flee to France

(Paris) Three Marxists from the Saarland, Mr. Braun, Mr. Woerther, and Mr. Haffmen, who were in favor of maintaining the status quo in the Saarland, fled to France today. According to Mr. Braun, he has no intention of returning to the Saarland. (National Telegram, 16th)

French Sarreguemines Residents of the Saarland who voted against returning the Saarland to Germany, fearing that they would not be able to protect themselves under Hitler's rule, have begun to migrate. Hundreds of people have arrived here today, and another 2,000 people will cross the border into France tomorrow. The police are now strictly checking the passports of those arriving here from the Saarland, and several people have been barred from entering the country because their passports did not meet the regulations. (Reuters, 16th)

Saarbrücken The Saarland Administrative Committee has received information from the French side that last night in Uting, several Saarland women, believing that their environment had been threatened, temporarily took refuge in Simbach, France. Shortly afterwards, they returned to the Saarland, and on the way, five people in uniform fired at them, fortunately without hitting them. It was later found by the French gendarmerie that the bullet casings had fallen within French territory. (Havas, 16th)

Hitler Attacks the Treaty of Versailles

Contradictory Statements

(Paris) German leader Hitler made a statement to American reporters yesterday, saying, "Once France can grant Germany equal rights, I am prepared to give up demands regarding territorial issues on France." This statement was reprinted by Paris Midi today and commented on by the newspaper's reporter, Schner, who said, "Hitler is using the Saarland plebiscite as a starting point to attack the Treaty of Versailles." After the results of Tuesday's plebiscite were announced, Hitler made a statement on the radio, saying that after the Saarland was returned to Germany, Germany would no longer make territorial demands on France. Now he has made contradictory statements to American reporters. His intentions are unpredictable. (Hannes, 17th)

Austrian Troops Increase Border Defense

Vienna The Austrian government, fearing that the results of the Saarland vote would cause demonstrations, today sent new troops to Linz in Upper Austria to strengthen the defenses on the border between Austria and Bavaria. At the same time, according to Reuters Berlin, the general manager of a steel factory in Zile, Saxony, Mr. Gort Beck, has been placed under protective custody at the request of the local National Socialist Party leader for not allowing his workers to listen to Hitler's speech during the Saarland vote. The factory has a total of 10,000 workers. (Reuters, 17th)

League of Nations Should Impose Arms Embargo on Paraguay

Subcommittee Submits Recommendation

Paraguay Threatens to Withdraw from the League

(Geneva) Regarding the Chaco dispute, the Advisory Committee of the League of Nations has received the report of the Subcommittee to impose sanctions on Paraguay, but Bolivia is not sanctioned because it has accepted the recommendations of the Special Assembly. Hu Shih-tse, the Chinese representative on the Chaco Committee, has advocated this approach from the beginning. (Central News Agency, 16th)

Asunción According to sources close to the government, if the League of Nations accepts the construction of the Advisory Committee and implements an arms embargo that favors Bolivia, Paraguay will withdraw from the League of Nations. According to the government's opinion, Bolivia is the head of the Chaco War, and any arms embargo that favors Bolivia violates the spirit and provisions of the League Covenant. (National Telegram, 16th)

(Washington) The dispute between Bolivia and Paraguay in South America over the Chaco territory has been pending for a long time. The League of Nations previously resolved to prohibit the shipment of arms to these two countries, and the United States also joined the embargo. The Advisory Committee of the Chaco Incident of the League of Nations has now submitted a report to the Advisory Committee, advocating that the ban on the transportation of arms to Bolivia be lifted, but Paraguay should still be embargoed for rejecting the recommendations passed by the League of Nations General Assembly last November to show sanctions. The United States is unlikely to consider this proposal, because the majority party leaders in Congress are not prepared for this. Senator Johnson and other senators who oppose the United States joining the League of Nations previously supported participating in the League of Nations' resolution to ban arms shipments because this ban applied to both belligerent countries. Now they declare that they do not want to allow this ban to be changed. The State Department may not take any action on this matter. Some informed sources believe that Bolivia bought arms from the United States during the implementation of the arms embargo, and was still able to buy them as usual after the implementation. The Ministry of Justice said that it has no power to force the people to respect this ban. (Havas, 16th)

Marseille Case, South Tyrol Dispute Included in Next Agenda

Italian-Albanian Dispute, the Two Countries Conduct Negotiations

(Geneva) Hungary has submitted a memorandum on the dispute between South Tyrol and Hungary over the Marseille assassination, stating the results of the investigation into the issue of responsibility for the case. Because the memorandum is too long, this session of the Council of the League of Nations has not been able to discuss it and will be handed over to the next session of the Council. (Havas, 16th)

(Geneva) The Albanian representative today applied to include the Italian-Albanian dispute over Ulzur in the agenda of this session of the Council of the League of Nations, but many believe that the representatives of the two countries in dispute are now conducting informal talks, the result of which may resolve the dispute without the League of Nations' intervention. (Reuters, 16th)

Poland Intends to Participate in the Non-Intervention Pact

Results of Talks Between French and Polish Foreign Ministers

Rome Agreement Presented to Austrian Government

(Geneva) Various important political talks are being conducted here today. According to Polish sources, French Foreign Minister Laval visited Polish Foreign Minister Beck and discussed various international issues and suggestions. According to reliable sources, the Polish Foreign Minister has agreed to participate in the Non-Intervention Pact proposed by Italy and France, but Poland still believes that there is no need to join the Eastern European Pact. The Polish Foreign Minister also met with Soviet Russian Foreign Affairs Commissioner Litvinov and Spanish representative Madariaga, and French Foreign Minister Laval also met with Soviet Russian Foreign Affairs Commissioner Litvinov. (National Telegram, 16th)

(Paris) The French government's response to Germany's memorandum of September 10th last year on the Eastern European Mutual Assistance Pact will not be published, but it is generally believed that today's meeting between Polish Foreign Minister Beck and French Foreign Minister Laval has brought the negotiations on the Eastern European Mutual Assistance Pact into a vigorous new stage. (Havas, 16th)

Vienna The Franco-Italian Non-Intervention Agreement has now been formally submitted to the Austrian government. The Austrian government hosted the diplomatic corps yesterday, and the French and Italian ambassadors to Austria personally handed over the Non-Intervention Agreement signed in Rome on January 17th to the Austrian Foreign Minister. (National Telegram, 17th)

US Secretary of the Navy Declares Maintenance of Current Ratio

Navy Aims to Complete Treaty Permitted Limits

(Washington) Secretary of the Navy Swanson declared today that the United States government has no other plans to immediately build new ships or renovate warships other than to complete the limits allowed by the treaty. Therefore, if a naval competition occurs internationally, the initiator must be another country, not the United States. Mr. Smith also said that he still advocates maintaining the current naval ratio. Secretary of War Germany declared that there is no need to dig a canal in Nicaragua, because the Panama Canal is sufficient to meet all needs. (National Telegram, 16th)

British Plan Air Route Between Rangoon and Hong Kong

Aviation Undersecretary's Mission to the Far East

(London) Sir Sassoon, Undersecretary of the Aviation Department, recently went to the Far East, and establishing an air route from Rangoon to Hong Kong is an important part of his mission. These negotiations are currently underway and must be agreed upon by Thailand, Vietnam, and China. At the same time, Imperial Airways is now considering adding several larger and faster aircraft to the India, Africa, and Australia routes in the hope that the promised one-and-a-half-penny Imperial airmail will become a reality in 1936. Currently, the amount of first-class mail sent to India every week is as much as ten tons, and Imperial Airways only carries one ton of it. (Reuters, 16th)

German Airline Plans Direct Flights to the Far East

Via Greece and India

The Hague Meeting to Avoid Competition

The Hague Major British, German, French, and Dutch airlines will meet here soon because the German Longsha Company is seeking to establish a direct air service from Berlin to Shanghai via India. It is said that the purpose of this meeting is to avoid unnecessary competition. Once the German government approves its plan, Longsha Company intends to conduct a test flight. The voyage is 14,000 kilometers long and will pass through Greece and India. (Reuters, 16th)

New German Postal Ship

Test Flight to the Far East This Summer

(Berlin) The new 18,000-ton ship Botsdan of the Hemy Company was launched in Hamburg today by General Friedrich, Mayor of Botsdan. The ship and the Scharnhorst, which was recently launched in front of German leader Hitler, are sister ships, 630 feet long and 72 feet wide, with a speed of approximately 20 knots per hour and can carry 300 passengers. It is scheduled to join the Far East class this summer. (Reuters, 16th)

Hamburg The new "Botsdan" postal ship of the German Hamburg America Shipping Company, which will sail to the Far East, was launched here today. The "Botsdan" will begin its test flight at the end of June and is expected to take only 23 days from the Italian port of Genoa to Shanghai. (Havas, 16th)

London Prepares to Hold a Chinese Art Exhibition

Treasures from the Forbidden City Will Be Shipped for Display

Chairman Lin and the King of England Serve as Honorary Presidents

(London) A large-scale Chinese art exhibition will be held in London from November 18th of this year to March 1936. After the Royal Academy of Fine Arts in the United Kingdom contacted the Chinese authorities, it plans to ship many of the antiquities from the Palace Museum in Peiping, which have not been seen by Europeans, to London for display. The exhibition will be co-hosted by the Chinese and British governments. The Chairman of the Chinese National Government, the King and Queen of England are all honorary presidents of the exhibition. Chinese cultural and artistic items from ancient times to 1800 years ago will be displayed separately. The Chinese government has allowed experts from the Chinese and British governments to jointly select antiquities from the Peiping Ancient Palace, including calligraphy, painting, ceramics, bronzes, jade, textiles, lacquerware, etc. In addition, collectors from Europe and the United States are invited to exhibit their rare treasures. Recent archaeological discoveries will also be displayed throughout the venue. It is generally hoped that this Chinese art exhibition, from an artistic point of view, can at least match previous international exhibitions, and Europe's understanding of Eastern art, especially Chinese art, will open a new era. (Havas, 16th)

(London) Four members of the organizing committee of the Chinese Art Exhibition will go to China, Japan, and the Americas this spring to discuss exhibition matters. (Havas, 17th)

El Salvador President Re-elected

Martínez Reelected

Central America, the capital of El Salvador El Salvador re-elected its president, and former President Martínez was re-elected. (Havas, 16th)

Current Affairs Commentary

Reflections on the Saar Plebiscite 　　Heng

The issue of the Saar's allegiance has been resolved due to the results of the 13th's plebiscite. The transfer of power and the establishment of a non-war zone afterward are minor details, not substantial issues, and not worth discussing. What I wish to say now is my own feelings.

The Saar is one of Europe's important coal regions. Its reserves, based on an annual output of 10 million tons, can be mined for 600 years without depletion. Moreover, before the Great War, the Germans used this coal to smelt the iron of Lorraine, so economically and technologically, it was almost inseparable from Lorraine. After the war, Lorraine was returned to France, so its desire to occupy the Saar was a matter of course. However, with the results of this plebiscite, the French authorities have been very open-minded about it, and do not want to raise any objections. This spirit of valuing promises, justice, and loving peace is truly worthy of our admiration. I believe that there are many causes of international hatred, but the forceful occupation of other people's land and the enslavement of other nations are the greatest causes. If all the countries in the world could deeply regret their territorial ambitions and respect the personality of others, then the precariousness and unease in international relations could be reduced by ninety percent. Without talking about peace, peace will come naturally. This is what I hope those who truly love peace will pay attention to.

Before the Saar plebiscite, those familiar with the international situation mostly predicted that a majority would return to Germany. However, the number of votes for returning to Germany was actually over 90 percent, which was quite unexpected. The reason is that since the German National Socialist Party revolution, the status quo faction has been quite active for a time due to the instigation and encouragement of various exiles. Because of this, outsiders did not dare to make a hasty judgment. Now, looking at the results of this plebiscite, we can see that what the people of the Saar want is national restoration. If they can restore their country, they can disregard all personal interests. This Germanic spirit, which prioritizes national interests, is truly worthy of being a model for our nation. Those status quo factions who only fight for the interests of their parties and individuals, and seek temporary comfort, deserve to be spurned by the people of the Saar.

The League of Nations governed the Saar for fifteen years, and there were many restrictions on the residents. However, the result was still a return to Germany. From this, we can see that anyone who uses force to invade other people's land will ultimately fail. This is a fact with many examples throughout history, both in China and abroad. The five barbarian tribes of the Jin Dynasty, the Liao, Jin, and Yuan dynasties after the Song Dynasty, and the Qing Dynasty after the Ming Dynasty, all had great momentum when they invaded our country. But in the end, they were all assimilated by us and could not harm us in the slightest. This is one example. Furthermore, evidence from modern European history also shows that this is always the case. Those who invade others inevitably fail, and those who are invaded, or even enslaved, have the possibility of national restoration, regardless of how long it takes. For example, the countries in the Balkan Peninsula were ruled by Turkey for hundreds of years, but in the nineteenth century, they successively became independent and autonomous. The same is true of Poland and the countries of the Little Entente. From this, we can see that as long as the national spirit exists, there will eventually be a day of revival. Those who like to invade others by force and enslave others only increase the animosity and hatred between nations and make world wars cycle endlessly.

Since the September 18th Incident, the spirit of our people has been extremely depressed. Everyone believes that the recovery of lost territory is an impossible fact. However, looking at the results of this Saar plebiscite, we can see that if the national spirit does not die, then lost territory can eventually be returned to the motherland. Therefore, what our country needs today is not pessimistic resignation, but vigorous self-improvement. We must first exhaust our intelligence and do our best to strengthen unity within the country and prioritize the interests of the nation, without being petty about personal interests. Then everything is possible, let alone the recovery of a small amount of lost territory. What is needed is whether the people of our country have a thorough awakening.

Roosevelt's Message to the Senate Urges Joining the World Court

Expresses Support for Peace While Not Harming U.S. Sovereignty

Asks Congress to Abandon Partisan Prejudices and Consider the Matter

(Washington) Senator Johnson today launched a major attack in the Senate on the issue of the United States joining the World Court. At the same time, President Roosevelt's message was read out, and Johnson immediately declared that he would do everything possible to keep all U.S. actions free and independent. He believes that the United States is being invited to participate in various disputes under the League of Nations system. As for President Roosevelt's message, it urges Congress to abandon partisan prejudices and consider the matter. The President also said, "The movement to promote international justice should be non-partisan. I sincerely hope that the Senate will pass the bill to join the World Court as soon as possible to realize this prudent and pure American policy." The President also stated that after joining, there is no danger of the United States' autonomy being harmed. "Moreover, at this time, international relations can all affect the future world peace, and it is an excellent opportunity for the United States to express its support for peace." Observers here expect that since the President has strongly advocated for the bill, the government's Senate leaders will exert great pressure on the opposition. (National Telegraph, 16th)

(Washington) Yesterday, President Roosevelt sent a message to the Senate recommending that the United States join the Permanent Court of International Justice at The Hague. Officials believe that the Senate will definitely pass it, because it was rumored beforehand that Roosevelt would not personally come forward on this matter. Now that the President has actually sent a message to the Senate, it shows that he is confident of success. Although some people in the United States are still strongly opposed to everything related to the International Court and the League of Nations, the fact that the Saar issue was resolved quickly and smoothly may be due to the League of Nations. American skeptics and opponents of the League of Nations have also been convinced by this. Recently, the Senate discussed the President's message. Senator Johnson, a Republican from California who usually supports the President but opposes joining the International Court, rose and said, "The International Court has nothing to do with the United States. If the United States joins, it will inevitably be drawn into the European vortex and will not be able to extricate itself." This is probably the biggest reason the opposition believes in. Fortunately, President Roosevelt had already anticipated this, and his message contained preemptive words, saying that successive Republican and Democratic governments in the United States had expressed approval of the International Court in principle. "This policy is very sound and consistent with the views of the American people. The sovereignty of the United States will in no way be weakened by this." (Havas Telegraph, 17th)

U.S. Senate Inflationists Convene Monetary System Conference

Negotiate a Specific Plan to Submit to Congress

Treasury Secretary Also Meets with the Attorney General

(Washington) The resolution passed by the National Monetary System Conference today has been submitted to Congress. The resolution advocates that the U.S. dollar should be detached from a fixed relationship with gold and abandon any similar gold standard situation in order to facilitate the U.S. response to foreign currency devaluation. The spokesperson of the conference also requested immediate minting of coins. (National Telegraph, 16th)

(Washington) The National Monetary System Conference convened by Senator Thomas, the leader of the Senate inflationists, opened today. First, representatives of several national organizations spoke, urging immediate devaluation of the U.S. currency. After a brief debate, a resolution was passed requesting that the U.S. dollar be restored to its 1926 purchasing power as soon as possible, and that a "U.S. Central Bank" be established to replace the Federal Reserve System and expand its power to control national lending. There are also other plans as follows: (1) Immediately pay veteran bonuses in cash; (2) Restore silver as the monetary standard, with free minting at a ratio of sixteen to one between gold and silver; (3) Reduce the gold content of the U.S. dollar again. Thomas delivered the opening speech, expressing hope that the attendees, representing half of the American people, would be able to jointly negotiate a specific plan to submit to Congress. Father Coughlin said that if Congress does not want to cause a revolution, it must restore its constitutionally granted power to control domestic currency prices, and said, "What we have now is just bookkeeping money." He also advocated that all Federal Reserve Banks should be nationalized. In addition, former Senator Owen represented the hard currency faction, advocating that Congress has the power to recover the right to adjust currency prices from private individuals. Congressional silver advocates such as Wheeler and Borah Martin also attended the meeting, but did not express their opinions. Silver advocates said that Thomas is most concerned with reducing the value of gold and the dollar and fighting for silver as the standard. In addition, paper money inflation is not what he wants to hear. (National Telegraph, 16th)

(Washington) The proposal committee of the National Inflation Conference today proposed to the conference to issue new coins so that veteran bonuses can be paid in full, and proposed to establish a central bank to control the national currency. According to its proposal, Congress will take over the minting power, regulate the currency, and have the power to deal with emergencies. The proposal committee does not advocate: (1) Creating a sound and sufficient currency that is detached from gold so that the country can deal with foreign currency manipulation; (2) Placing the U.S. currency value in a position that can at least restore 1926 prices. Today, the temporary meeting between Treasury Secretary Morgenthau and Attorney General Cummings has aroused speculation that the authorities may have new financial measures. (Reuters Telegraph, 16th)

(Washington) Officialdom here firmly believes that the Supreme Court will uphold the abolition of gold clauses, but if the court rules unfavorably to the issue, the authorities will submit a legislative bill to legalize President Roosevelt's move to abolish gold clauses. President Roosevelt's attempt to raise prices by reducing the gold content of the U.S. dollar is an extremely important part of the President's program, and the success or failure of this move depends on the invalidation of the gold clauses in June 1933. Therefore, if the court makes a ruling unfavorable to the government, President Roosevelt will inevitably try to avoid the consequences arising therefrom, because he does not want his new measures to be in danger of being overturned. At a time when the people are eagerly awaiting the court's decision, the inflationists have gathered here to negotiate a plan to make the U.S. dollar even cheaper. Senator Thomas has convened representatives of various organizations that support inflation and members of Congress to meet. This meeting is called the National Inflation Conference. Thomas announced that the purpose of this meeting is to obtain a cheaper U.S. dollar in order to restore 1926 prices. Senator Wheeler stated that various currency plans will depend on the Supreme Court's decision on whether securities containing gold clauses must be paid with old U.S. dollars or with current U.S. dollars. Once the verdict is announced, the authorities will take practical steps to deal with it. No matter what the court does, there is nothing to worry about, because Congress can immediately legislate to deal with the situation arising therefrom. The general opinion in financial circles is that the activities of the inflationists are enough to confirm the speculation that President Roosevelt would rather disobey the Supreme Court than re-raise the price of the U.S. dollar. At the same time, trading in the New York stock market is currently quite quiet, because it wants to wait for the result of the gold clause case. (Reuters Telegraph, 17th)

Roosevelt's Old-Age Pensions and Poverty Relief

(Washington) The U.S. government today implemented two major relief measures for the issue of old-age pensions and poverty relief:

(1) Providing unemployed people with a weekly subsidy of $15;

(2) Providing elderly people with a monthly old-age pension of $15 to $60.

This bill has been submitted to the House of Representatives by Senator Wagner. (National Telegraph, 17th)

France Ships Gold to the United States

(Paris) France is now shipping gold to the United States again because it has received news from Washington that the U.S. authorities do not want to change the U.S. gold price. U.S. officials are confident that the Supreme Court will support the authorities in the gold clause case, but even if the court recognizes the abolition of gold clauses as illegal, the authorities will try to circumvent it. France and the United States both hold a kind of trust that President Roosevelt will try to overcome any legal obstacles encountered by his monetary policy. This situation can be seen in today's Reuters telegraph. (Reuters Telegraph, 16th)

(Paris) After receiving news from the U.S. Treasury Department that it does not want to lower the gold price, French bankers are now preparing to load more gold to go to the United States. The first batch will be loaded on the German ship Europa on Saturday and Sunday to cross the Atlantic. (Reuters Telegraph, 17th)

Polish Senate Passes New Constitution Draft

Abolishes the Name of the Republic

Cancels Proportional Representation

Warsaw The Polish Senate recently passed the new constitution draft with a majority of 74 votes to 24. One of the most important aspects of this new constitution is that the name "Polish Republic" is no longer in the constitution, only "Polish State." The proportional representation system has been completely abolished. As for the new election law, it is not included in the constitution and will be submitted and passed separately later. The general rights of citizens are still maintained in the new constitution, but some are restricted. In addition, what the opposition party members are particularly uneasy about is the autonomous system of Upper Silesia, because according to the new constitution, the autonomous system of Upper Silesia can be changed or completely abolished only after the State Council decides. After this new constitution draft is passed in the Senate, it will be submitted to the House of Representatives for discussion starting next week. The House of Representatives only needs a majority to pass the constitution draft. (Note: Upper Silesia originally belonged to Germany, and part of it was划归to Poland after the European War) (Havas Telegraph, 16th)

Japan-Russia Negotiations

(Tokyo) The Sino-Eastern Railway issue, which has been under negotiation for two years since the start of negotiations, can be satisfactorily resolved after two or three more consultations. Foreign Minister Hirota is determined to take this opportunity to resolve various pending issues between Japan and Russia in order. After Ambassador Ota returns to Russia, he will immediately start negotiations with the Russian government on the revision of the Japan-Russia Fisheries Treaty, and negotiate the establishment of a committee to prevent border wars, the North Sakhalin oil rights issue, etc. (Japan United Telegraph, 17th)

(Moscow) Moscow newspapers all carried the following Harbin news: A Harbin newspaper reported that the Soviet Deputy Consul in Harbin, Trepinsky, had a conversation with a "certain important person in Manchuria," falsely claiming that Trepinsky had said, "Whether the Sino-Eastern Railway issue can be resolved is doubtful, because the Soviet Union has not been eager to sell the railway recently," etc. The intention of this rumor is very obvious, that is, the Soviet Union does not want to sell the railway, so the Tokyo talks must be stopped, and at the same time, the railway must be forcibly seized by force. The Soviet Consulate General in Harbin issued a denial of this, pointing out that this is purely fabricated. However, the Manchurian semi-official news agency Guotongshe claimed that although the Consulate General denied it, "reliable sources" proved that Trepinsky's conversation was indeed true. The Soviet side made an oral protest to Guotongshe, and the "Manchukuo" Foreign Affairs Bureau replied that it had no say in Guotongshe, because the latter had extraterritorial rights and was under the jurisdiction of the Japanese. These Japanese are not subject to the control of the Manchurian authorities because they have consular jurisdiction. (Tass Telegraph, 16th)

British Liberal Party Leader Announces Major Economic Recovery Plan

Advocates British-American Cooperation to Guarantee World Peace

Actively Use Tariffs to Eliminate Trade Barriers

Organize Public Works to Absorb Domestic Unemployment

Declares It Is Purely for the Country and Does Not Want to Promote Doctrines

Former Chancellor of the Exchequer Snowden Expresses Strong Support

(London) Liberal Party leader Lloyd George took the opportunity of his 72nd birthday today to address the public at a gathering in Bangor, announcing his major plan to relieve the British economic difficulties. Although George is old, his speech was as impassioned and fluent as ever, so he was able to attract the attention of thousands of listeners in attendance. It is estimated that no less than 5,000 people stood outside in the cold wind listening to his speech through loudspeakers. The number of people who came from all over Wales by special car to listen to the speech was unprecedented. Although George did not criticize the party system at the beginning of his speech, he said that political parties are indeed useful in ordinary times, but his advance has no party nature at all.

George detailed the collapse of the world economic system and said that although there had been predictions that trade in Britain was about to recover, in 1934 our country's trade deficit reached the highest record in peacetime. If Britain has a more courageous foreign policy in diplomacy and commerce, then commerce will definitely improve, and those who can absorb temporary unemployment, all undertakings that can increase national assets, can absorb permanent unemployment. The finances required for this plan should be limited to assets that can be raised annually without harming ordinary commercial operations. He believes that it can prosper the country's debt, and will definitely be happily purchased by the public. National credit should not be used too much. The previous plans of the Bank of England can be said to be misleading, short-sighted and leave future troubles. He is not saying that the Bank of England should be a part of the government, but that the directors of the bank should be carefully selected to have closer contact with industry and commerce. He can nationalize banks that will be established jointly. George then briefly outlined his plan as follows: (1) British-American cooperation to guarantee world peace; (2) Actively use Britain's tariffs and other negotiation tools to eliminate international trade barriers; (3) Organize real public undertakings to absorb permanently unemployed people and settle more people in farming; (4) Establish a committee with power but no party nature to plan and implement the plan, and raise funds; (5) Organize a committee of five cabinet members according to the wartime cabinet method to constantly consider domestic and foreign policy issues. (Reuters Telegraph, 17th)

(London) Former Labour cabinet Chancellor of the Exchequer Snowden published a letter to Liberal Party leader Lloyd George. This letter has aroused great attention in political circles, because Snowden's letter contains the intention of supporting George. Snowden said that the movement advocated by George that the whole country should make great efforts to prosper industry and relieve the people's poverty should be supported by the electors. George will give a speech in Bangor today to explain his new plan to prosper the country, and Snowden's letter was published last night. Snowden said that the people have been waiting for a long time to get a leader who can carry out a great national plan. If the country's efforts are spent on waste, and if the great power of Britain is organized and actively used, then unemployment can definitely be eradicated, and the high living standards of labor can also be achieved. He can see it put into practice and solve this problem. In between, Mr. Shi will sometimes give speeches in the same place as George. George will announce his new plan in September, but I will explain that the methods he intends are by no means political and party-based, and he does not want to promote liberalism, socialism, capitalism, or any other doctrine, but a sincere contribution to solving the current great difficulties. The national management of the Bank of England is a part of his plan, but not all of it. After the details are published, the people will be able to judge before the next election. He intends that a general election may be held within the next eighteen months. It is said that Snowden was the mainstay of the MacDonald Labour cabinet. Later, because MacDonald agreed to cooperate with the Conservative Party, Shi resigned and went into opposition. Lloyd George was the British Prime Minister during the war and is one of the most prestigious figures in British political circles. (Reuters Telegraph, 17th)

Disposition of Estate of British Press Tycoon Rothermere

Nearly Two Million Pounds Sterling

Donated for Charitable Purposes

(London) The estate of Lord Rothermere, the well-known newspaper owner, was certified today to total £1,839,000, with taxes payable of approximately £784,021. The will donates a large sum of money for charitable purposes and makes gifts to prominent men and women in society and former employees. George, who was the Prime Minister during the European War, and Churchill, a prominent figure in British political circles, were each given £1,000. It was also found that his will used one-third of the estate's profits to fund the news publishing fund, another one-third to help the Royal Free Hospital, one-sixth to fund the printing workers' pension fund, and the remaining one-sixth to be divided equally by two certain organizations. (Reuters Telegraph, 16th)

Hebei Provincial River Affairs Conference Opens

(Tianjin) The Hebei Provincial River Affairs Conference opened at 10:00 a.m. today in the auditorium of the Construction Department. Yu Xue-zhong, Civil Affairs Director Zhang Hou-wan, Finance Director Lu Mu-ting, Construction Director Hu Yuan-hui, Education Director Zheng Dao-ru, Provincial Committee Member Cha Yao, and more than 50 river bureau directors and water conservancy experts attended. He said that he has been in Hebei for three years, and there have been floods for two years. If the Yellow River is in danger again this year, and the Yongding River has no solution, it would be too unfair to the people of Hebei. He hopes that everyone will work hard and invigorate. He will also personally inspect the rivers. If there is any negligence, he will break through sentiment and strictly handle it. The ceremony ended at noon. Tianxi Commemorative Stele Discovered in Nanjing

(Nanjing) The Nanjing Historical Site Investigation Association recently discovered a historical site called the Tianxi Commemorative Stele, also known as the Tianfa Shenchan, which was built by Sun Hao of the Eastern Wu during the Three Kingdoms period. A portion was destroyed during the Ming Dynasty, and it was further damaged by a major fire during the Hongyang Rebellion and buried underground. The association has scheduled a meeting on the 18th, inviting various cultural institutions and the municipal government to discuss excavation methods. (Central News Agency telegram, 17th)

International Commercial Telegram

丨Reuters Special Commercial News Telegram, January 17th丨

Gold and Silver

London Gold Price: Today is 141 shillings and 11 pence, up 5 pence.

London Silver Market: Today's price rose 0.0625, spot price is 24 pence 625, futures price is 24 pence 75. India purchased, speculators sold, and trading was thin.

Bombay Silver Market: Today was quiet, spot price at closing was 64 rupees and 10 annas, down 1 anna.

Exchange Rates

British-American: The London foreign exchange market has been very volatile recently, but the market was calm this morning, with little fluctuation. The British-American exchange rate opened at 4 dollars 87 and 75 cents, the same as yesterday's American-British closing price. After falling to 4 dollars 87 and 6875 cents once, the price rose again to 4 dollars 87 and 9375 cents, which is the most recent price. Also, 1 US dollar equals 4 shillings 1 penny 186 British gold.

British-French: Opened unchanged at 74 francs 28. This price has not changed until the time of the telegram.

American-British: The New York foreign exchange market is gradually returning to normal today. The American-British exchange rate opened at 4 dollars 88 and 25 cents, up half a cent. Within an hour of opening, there were occasional fluctuations, but not far from this price. The American-French exchange rate was firmer, opening at 6 dollars 57 and 875 cents, up 1 cent and 125.

Cotton and Wheat

New York Cotton: The allocation of the Penhaid cotton field quota will be announced by the Department of Agriculture at 11 am this morning, so the focus of the cotton market is mostly on this. The opening was stable, and industry demand remained good, so the price rose, about 25 cents per bale. After the price rose, selling pressure increased sharply, and the price quickly fell back to yesterday's closing price.

New York Wheat: The wheat market opened relatively stable, but unpredictable. Prices changed little from yesterday's close. The weather report was unfavorable, and the cold was even more severe in the winter wheat region.

Bombay Cotton: Today's cotton market saw sellers covering shorts, absorbing long positions being liquidated. The closing price for April-May White Rose cotton was 241 rupees and 7 annas, up 1 anna.

Liverpool Wheat: The wheat market this morning had a more stable trend. At 1 pm, the May price rose half a penny to 5 shillings and 025.

Liverpool Cotton: The cotton market today was firmer. At 1 pm, the May price was 6.82, up 3 points.

Rubber

London: The market was quiet this morning. At noon, the transaction price for April-June was 6 pence 5625, the same as yesterday's closing price.

New York: The opening price rose 6 points today, but the price fell slightly due to retail sales.

Securities

New York: The factors favorable to the market before the securities opening were that yesterday's movement in the securities market could be seen as a calmer attitude among market participants before the Gold Clause decision. Short positions have recently increased greatly, so the market is expected to improve due to increased confidence. Coupled with good commercial news, the market is gradually looking good. The unfavorable factor for the market is the uncertainty of the Gold Clause issue, which still has a limited impact on trading. The securities market opened sluggish but stable this morning, with most securities slightly up. The Gold Clause case still makes people uneasy, so the market seems to have a sluggish and narrow trend today.

According to a Reuters report, although the Gold Clause dispute is still an important factor on Wall Street this morning, the market was able to calm down yesterday, and morale improved as a result. The securities exchange's base is strong, as is the same for other markets. Speakers therefore expect that prices in the stock market may gradually improve this morning. After the market opened this morning, trading was still not active, but most stocks were slightly higher.
