Japanese Business Inspection Group Visits Lianyungang

Returns via Xuzhou and West to Xi'an Before Returning East

Situation Upon Arrival at Xinpu

Xinpu News: The Qingdao Japanese Chamber of Commerce and Industry Inspection Group, led by Hiraoka Kotaro, a party of eighteen people, arrived in Xinpu on the 12th, visited Lianyungang on the 13th, and went to Xuzhou on the 14th. They are scheduled to travel west to Xi'an on the 15th. The following is a record of the group's departure and visit.

The inspection group of eighteen members is led by Hiraoka Kotaro, director of the Japanese Textile Industry Association in China. The other seventeen members include Kōichi Kamiya of Fukusho Company, Masamori Man'i of Daido Yōshi Store, Ikutarō Tanabe of Iwaki Shōkai, Setsuzō Imazawa of Yokohama Specie Bank, Tetsu Takahashi of Dairyo Rubber Factory, and Ichiji Higo, etc., six people as Group A. Except for Ichiji Higo, who went south to Beijing to visit Okano when he was in Xuzhou, the rest all went north back to Qingdao. Kin'ichi Yamamuro of Zuifeng Cotton Store, Takayuki Maeda of Okura Yōkō, Haruhito Asai of Asai Shōten, Setsuji Uchida of Ryūkō Textile Factory, Yōshaku Suetake of Suetake Shōten, Masahisa Kawai of Nikka Sanshi Kai, Yasuyoshi Shiraishi of Shiraishi Yōkō, Iwao Ogawa of Shōwa Yōkō, Tadao Shimazu and Kōkō Izawa of Qingdao Chamber of Commerce and Industry, and Takeo Mizuno of Mitsui Bussan, together with the leader Hiraoka Kotaro, twelve people as Group B, plan to visit Xi'an, Zhengzhou, and Tianjin before returning within the month. Except for Mizuno Takeo, who departed from Qingnan, the other seventeen people all claimed to have come from Qingdao. All eighteen members of the inspection group hold passports issued by the Japanese consuls in Qingdao or Jinan, with a two-month validity period. Before the inspection began, Qingdao Mayor Shen Honglie telegraphed the Guanyun County Government and other local governments along the way to send personnel to greet and escort them. The group departed from Qingdao on the Jiaoji Railway on the 10th, stayed overnight in Jinan, and on the 11th, took the Jinpu Railway south. They arrived in Xuzhou on the morning of the 12th, where they were greeted by personnel from the Xuzhou local government, and immediately transferred to the Longhai Railway eastward. At Xin'anzhen, they were replaced by personnel from the coastal local government for escort. At half past four in the afternoon, the train arrived in Xinpu. Because it was already dark, it was inconvenient to go ahead, so they stayed in Xinpu at the Datong Hotel.

At half past six on the morning of the 13th, the group of eighteen people, escorted by personnel from the coastal local government, took the Longhai Railway train to Laoyao at ten o'clock. In front of Laoyao were the No. 1 and No. 2 piers of Lianyungang, which were under construction. They were led by Zhang Jiechao, director of the Port Affairs Office of the Longhai Railway Administration, and Dong Yaotang, chief of the western section, to visit the pier. The No. 2 pier is nearing completion, and two ships are already berthed on the west bank. The No. 1 pier is being paved with stones, and the Henan Company, which is contracting the project, is busy transporting stones with small trains. The members of the inspection group paid close attention to the water depth, high terrain, import and export goods, and local commerce. Cotton was of particular interest to the Japanese, who tore the cotton by hand to test the length of its fibers. Hiraoka Kotaro intended to see Mr. Hamm, the director of the port construction, but was unable to find him because it was a Sunday. Due to the short time, they did not have time to go up the mountain and enter the town, so at eleven o'clock, they took the train eastward and arrived in Xinpu at two o'clock in the afternoon.

From Xinpu Station to the Datong Hotel in the street, the local government provided four cars for the inspection group to use. When the car arrived in front of the Datong Hotel, Kin'ichi Yamamuro and three others got out of the car and asked the local government personnel to allow the entire group to take the original car to Dapū, their intention was very firm at first. After the local government personnel repeatedly informed them that the road was muddy due to rain, making it inconvenient for the car to travel, and that there were many bandits in the countryside, fearing accidents, they stopped. The inspection group then entered the hotel to rest. After a short rest, Hiraoka Kotaro and Ichiji Higo requested to visit the airfield, which they immediately did. In addition, eleven people, including Yasuyoshi Shiraishi, visited the river, while two others went to visit the street.

Because they were busy visiting during the day and did not have time to eat, they had their meal at four o'clock in the afternoon. After the meal, they rested at the hotel.

At forty minutes past eleven on the morning of the 14th, the inspection group of eighteen people took a car to Xuzhou. The six people in Group A took the Jinpu Railway train to various places in the north and south that day. Group B scheduled to travel west to Xi'an on the 15th.

According to Hiraoka Kotaro and Kin'ichi Yamamuro, Lianyungang seems a bit small. When the two piers are completely completed, they can only berth six ships of 3,000 tons or less, which cannot be compared to the Qingdao pier, which can berth more than 25 ships of 10,000 tons or more. But it is still a good port for handling goods. Lianyungang is close to Qingdao, and they should cooperate and promote communication between commercial ships to seek the development of Sino-Japanese trade, and so on.

Situation Passing Through Xuzhou

Xuzhou Correspondence: Japanese residents in Qingdao, recognizing that the Longhai Railway, connecting the Central Plains, opening the port of Lianyungang to the east, and reaching Chang'an to the west, has a tendency to replace Qingdao in terms of geographical advantages, and that the railway also occupies an important position in national defense and commerce, have organized the Longhai Railway Lianyungang Industrial and Commercial Inspection Group, a party of eighteen people. The head of the group is Hiraoka Kotaro, director of the Japanese Textile Manufacturers Association in China, and Izawa Kimiyuki, head of the Qingdao Japanese Chamber of Commerce and Industry, is assisting in the arrangements. The group departed from Qingdao via Jinan to Xuzhou on the 12th, and then traveled east by train. Local administrative authorities received a telegram from the provincial government in advance to provide adequate protection. The Administrative Commissioner's Office dispatched Yu Keyu, the County Government dispatched Chen Jiesan, and the Public Security Bureau dispatched Zhao Yiqian to accompany the group. The Longhai Railway Bureau also dispatched General Section Chief Dong Yaotang to accompany and entertain the group. The group arrived in Xinpu on the evening of the 12th. On the morning of the 13th, the Longhai Railway prepared a special train to transport the group to various places such as Xugou Sunjiashan Lao Yao for sightseeing. In particular, they inquired in detail about the depth of the sea in the Lao Yao port, the draft of the ships, and the height of the mountains, and observed them on the map separately. At that time, they also planned to take photos, but the accompanying administrative staff politely dissuaded them. They expressed dissatisfaction with this obstruction. That evening, they returned to Xinpu by train. Due to the rain and muddy roads, the journey was inconvenient. On the morning of the 14th, they took the Longhai Express train west again, arriving in Xuzhou at 8:30 that night.

After the group arrived in Xuzhou and got off the train, they were guided by local government officials to stay at the Huayuan Hotel. In addition to most of the group heading west for inspection, group member Higo took the Jinpu train south that evening to go to the capital for business. In addition, group members Takahashi, Murai, Okaba, Imazawa, and Kamiya, five people in total, took the train north back to Jinan at 6:30 on the morning of the 15th. The majority of the group, led by Hiraoka, toured various scenic spots in Xuzhou on the morning of the 15th and inspected the commercial market situation, and went to various foreign goods firms to investigate the sales volume of Japanese goods, and at the same time made preparations for supply.

After the group arrived in Xuzhou and before leaving Xuzhou on the 15th, the reporter visited them twice. Hiraoka Kotaro and Izawa Kimiyuki were elected by the group to receive the reporter. The reporter asked them about the purpose of this inspection and their impressions after visiting Xuzhou and Lianyungang. They replied that they had been engaged in industry and commerce in Qingdao for more than ten years and had rarely traveled to the Chinese mainland. Taking advantage of the slack season at the end of the year and the beginning of the year, they organized the Longhai Railway inspection group to visit the seaports along the eastern section to the west. Lianyungang is very close to Qingdao and is related to the famous commercial ports in the East. After inspection, they praised the greatness of the port's construction. However, they felt that the Lao Yao wharf was located at the foot of the mountain and could not be developed. In the future, the construction of houses would be quite limited, and it seemed that it could not be fully developed. The Lao Yao wharf for loading and unloading goods was also narrow. Compared with Shanghai and Qingdao, it was slightly inferior, but it was located between the two ports and had a great relationship in connecting the ports. They came here and planned to engage in business within the possible range. This trip to the west was intended to stop in Zhengzhou and Luoyang for sightseeing, and then go straight to Xi'an, and after a few days in An Xun, they would return to Qingdao via Zhengjing Beiping.

The group toured Xuzhou for half a day and left Xuzhou on the 15th at 12:40 noon, taking the Longhai Westbound Special Express train to Zhengzhou. Their original plan was to get off the train in Kaifeng, but later decided to go straight to Luoyang. If there were Japanese residents waiting for them in Zhengzhou, they planned to get off the train there, otherwise they would stop in Luoyang. They also planned to visit Mount Hua when they arrived in Huayin. They planned to stay in Xi'an for three days and then return east and then to Beiping. According to the administrative staff accompanying the group, the group paid close attention to the geographical situation in the places they visited, and often asked where the airfield was, where the barracks were, and where the fortress area was. Their actions did not seem like a simple tour and inspection, according to the Central News Agency.

Major Panic in Xiamen's Financial World

Three Major Money Houses Collapse in Five Days

Xiamen Commercial Bank Also Closes

Xiamen Correspondence: After the New Year, a major panic suddenly broke out in Xiamen's financial world. In one week, the three major money houses of Huang Jianyuan, Yu Feng, and Yinjiang collapsed one after another. Jianyuan and Yu Feng had been established for more than 20 years, had a good reputation, and the most abundant capital, and were the largest and most famous money houses in Xiamen. Unexpectedly, on the 12th, Xiamen's only Xiamen Commercial Bank also announced its closure.

On January 6, Yinjiang Money House on Shuixian Road announced its closure. Manager Li Zhai went into hiding, owing people 170,000 to 180,000 yuan, deposits of more than 200,000 yuan, and owing banks more than 100,000 yuan, with a total debt of about 500,000 yuan. On the 9th, Huang Jianyuan, a famous money house in Xiamen, also ran aground. Huang Jianyuan was operated by Huang Shijin, a wealthy businessman in Xiamen. Huang's operations included Jianyuan Bank, Jianfeng Grocery, and Jiansheng Pawnshop, and also engaged in savings mortgages. All had been open for decades and had a good reputation in Xiamen. Hong Kong had a branch called Jianyuan Zhan, and Shanghai had Jianji Remittance Bank. After Yinjiang closed, Jianyuan suddenly experienced a run. Huang planned to mortgage 500,000 yuan of assets to the Bank of China for 200,000 yuan to cope with the situation, but unfortunately it failed, and he announced a shutdown. Jiansheng Pawnshop was also trapped in a shutdown. Deposits and debts totaled more than 1.2 million yuan, and all assets and debts owed could be offset. For a time, people were shocked, and the financial storm expanded further. On the 10th, Yu Feng Money House, operated by Liao Yuefa, a leader in the city's money house industry, whose capital and reputation were comparable to Jianyuan, also stopped business because it could not cope with depositors' withdrawals. Debts also reached more than 1 million yuan. In total, the three houses collapsed in succession in five days, with debts reaching more than 2.5 million yuan, and people were even more panicked. On the 12th, Xiamen's only Xiamen Commercial Bank also suspended business due to withdrawals. Xiamen Commercial Bank was established in the 11th year of the Republic, with a capital of 600,000 yuan, and later increased by 60,000 yuan, totaling 660,000 yuan. It had a branch in Shanghai and an office in Ningbo, and had a good reputation. On Saturday the 12th, the treasury had only more than 40,000 yuan in stock. The depositors continued to arrive after the bank opened at nine o'clock. Manager Ouyang Ze, seeing that Jianyuan and Yu Feng had closed successively in two days, and that Huang Shijin, a shareholder of Jianyuan, and Liao Yuefa, a shareholder of Yu Feng, were both directors of Xiamen Bank, was already wary. On the one hand, he first borrowed money from Huang Boquan, president of the Bank of China (also a director of Xiamen Bank), Huang Qinshu, president of the Bank of Communications (also a director of Xiamen Bank), and Ye Tianxuan, president of Zhongxing Bank, to maintain the situation. Huang (Qinshu) and Ye initially agreed. Ouyang then ordered the staff to silently record the number of withdrawals on the morning of the 12th, promising to pay them later. He went to the two banks to urge the loans, but the loan matter suddenly changed. Those waiting to withdraw money at Xiamen Bank had more than 30,000 yuan by 10:30, and suddenly increased to 70,000 to 80,000 yuan at 11:00. The treasury had only more than 40,000 yuan in stock, which was not enough to pay. He announced that payments would be temporarily suspended until Monday, the 14th, to resolve the issue. The bank convened a board meeting on the 13th, which was a Sunday. Huang Yizhu (represented by Huang Yishou), Liao Yuefa (represented by Wu Shihan), Chen Qingbo, Zeng Shangyuan, Huang Boquan, Chen Yitang, Shen Jinting, Zhang Naiping, Huang Zhitin, and Huang Qinshu attended the meeting and resolved to "temporarily suspend business for 15 days from the 14th, and convene a temporary shareholders' meeting on the 30th of this month to resolve everything." The board of directors hired lawyer Du Baoqi and accountant Wang Yunyu to handle legal and accounting matters. On the morning of the 14th, the bank posted a notice, which read, "Due to the tight financial situation in the market, the bank has temporarily suspended business for 15 days after a resolution by the board of directors, pending the convening of a temporary shareholders' meeting in accordance with Article 16, Section 2 of the bank's articles of association to resolve all matters. January 14, 24th year." It also submitted a report to the Public Security Bureau, which read, "Recently, due to the tight money supply in the market, all loans have not been recovered, and all deposits have been withdrawn due to the impact of withdrawals from various money houses. Business has been temporarily suspended for 15 days after a resolution by the board of directors to convene a shareholders' meeting to resolve the issue. During this period, the accounts will be sorted out and reported to the meeting. Please send police to protect the bank," etc.

It is rumored that Xiamen Bank absorbed more than 4 million yuan in deposits. According to Liu Yunsong, deputy manager of the bank, "Xiamen Bank has temporarily suspended business due to a temporary cash flow problem. The Shanghai branch and the Ningbo office under the Shanghai branch will not be suspended. The Shanghai branch has sent a telegram requesting instructions and has replied that it will handle the situation as it sees fit. The bank's deposits reached more than 3 million yuan at the peak. In recent years, the market has been sluggish and the money supply has been tight, and more than half of the deposits have been withdrawn. The current fixed-term and current deposits are more than 1.5 million yuan, plus more than 2 million yuan in transactions with various counterparts. The bank's assets are sufficient to offset the debts," etc.

The biggest reason for the financial turmoil in Xiamen this time is that the price of gold has soared in the past three years, and commerce in Nanyang has declined. Overseas Chinese in Nanyang have no business to operate, and the exchange rate is high, so they are competing to remit money back to China. However, the hometowns of the overseas Chinese in southern Fujian have been plagued by bandits for years, and they dare not invest in the mainland. This large amount of capital returning to the country is concentrated in Xiamen, and its channels for disposal are (1) investing in real estate and building municipal houses, and (2) depositing in banks and money houses. Xiamen has been building roads and new markets for only a few years, and the construction is all new. The buildings are lined up and there is almost no space, and most of them are four-story steel frames, and the construction is very sophisticated, all of which is the capital of overseas Chinese. As a result, land prices in Xiamen soared two years ago. For example, the old site of Guandi Temple on Datong Road rose to 4,000 yuan per square foot. The rent is so high that a three- or four-story building on Zhongshan Datong Road that is only 1.2 feet wide costs more than 200 yuan per month. In addition to investing in real estate, they deposit in banks and money houses. Last summer, the Chamber of Commerce investigated and found that the deposits received by various banks reached more than 40 million yuan. Although the number of deposits received by money houses is unknown, it can be known that it exceeds the number of banks. In recent years, the market has been sluggish, and stores are competing to hold low-price sales, but few people care. As a result, closures are common, and municipal houses are empty. As a result, land prices have plummeted, and the money industry is unable to recover loans. For example, the price of a square foot on Datong Road that was sold for 4,000 yuan before is now 800 yuan and no one cares. Tenants are competing to reduce rents. Monthly rents of more than 200 yuan have fallen to more than 100 yuan, and there are still many vacant buildings along Zhongshan Shengping Road. Banks and money houses absorb deposits and invest a lot in real estate. Since no one cares about real estate and houses, cash is therefore dead. At the same time, the money supply is extremely tight, and there are many withdrawals, so exhaustion appears. It also happened to be near the end of the lunar year, and there was a great need for cash. No one was willing to accept mortgages on real estate and houses, and the lending merchants were unable to recover their loans, so Jianyuan and Yu Feng collapsed, and the repercussions became a major wave. Xiamen Commercial Bank had no choice but to be involved. On the 13th, the Xiamen Chamber of Commerce sent a letter to the city, stating that the financial panic in the city was becoming increasingly dangerous, and that a joint meeting would be held this afternoon (the 14th) at 2:00 pm, inviting local authorities such as the Public Security Bureau, the Siming County Magistrate, the presidents of various banks, various trade associations, and all members of the executive and supervisory committees of the chamber to discuss relief measures. At present, people are still very agitated, and we are waiting for the results of the joint meeting to shift the situation. (January 14)

Fujian Provincial Pacification Conference

Fourteen Commanders and Division Commanders Attended

Sixty-Seven Proposals Passed in Two-Day Meeting

Zhangzhou Correspondence: Jiang Dingwen, the special envoy for pacification stationed in Fujian, considering that the pacification mission was heavy and in order to pool ideas, returned to Zhangzhou from the province on the 4th of this month and telegraphed all commanders of subordinate districts and division commanders stationed in Fujian to Zhangzhou to hold a provincial pacification conference to decide on all operational guidelines and implementation steps. The conference opened on the morning of the 10th and closed on the afternoon of the 11th. Four meetings were held in two days, and 67 proposals were passed. The details of the process are recorded below.

Attendees

The attendees were Li Yannan, Commander of the 11th Pacification Zone, Wang Jingjiu, Commander of the 12th Pacification Zone, Wang Jicheng, representative of Liu Heding, Commander of the 9th Pacification Zone (Chief of Staff of the Command), Guo Jiqiao, representative of Wei Lihuang, Commander of the 10th Pacification Zone (Chief of Staff of the Command), Li Yutang, Commander of the 3rd Division, Peng Shuru, Deputy Commander of the 10th Division, Zhang Yiyang, representative of the 36th Division, Dai Minquan, Commander of the 45th Division, Lu Xingrong, Commander of the 52nd Division, Chen Qi, Commander of the 80th Division, Liu Kan, Commander of the 83rd Division, Shi Honglie, Deputy Commander of the 87th Division, and Ding Jianfan, Deputy Commander of the New 11th Division, etc., totaling 14 people. Li Jianai, Chief of Staff of the Pacification Headquarters, Zhang Jiong, Chief Advisor, and Shao Qiyong, Tian Xiyuan, Wang Qibo, Feng Chizhong, Yang Huaidang, and Li Yi, directors of various departments, also attended the meeting.

Meeting Details

The meeting venue was set up in the main hall on the third floor of the Pacification Headquarters. The first meeting opened at 10:00 am on the 10th. After performing the ceremonial formalities, Chairman Jiang Dingwen delivered the opening remarks, which read, "Gentlemen, we entered Fujian from Jiangxi in the 22nd year of the Republic to suppress bandits and quell rebellions. After a year, we have finally come to an end. During this year, because you were all on the front lines and had your own missions, we did not have the opportunity to gather together. Now we have entered the pacification period, and although the situation is more relaxed, the mission has become more onerous. In order to easily achieve the goal of pacification, I have specially invited you to the headquarters to conduct in-depth discussions. Now, I will first report the important tasks and significance of pacification as follows. The task of pacification is first to eliminate scattered bandits in the shortest possible time. This is without a doubt. Now that the national crisis is deep and the people's difficulties have not been relieved, it is not enough to talk about internal peace if the scattered bandits are not eliminated, and it is not enough to resist foreign aggression. To eliminate scattered bandits, it is even more necessary to complete transportation, organize the people, handle the aftermath of bandit areas, and reorganize local teams, all at the same time, as a fundamental solution. As for the people's armed forces in various places, Fujian has a special situation, and the number is particularly large. Most of them have been loyal to the party and the country and participated in the revolutionary movement. We also intend to work with Chairman Chen to conduct a thorough verification and separately reorganize them into provincial security regiments and county security teams, and actively reorganize and train them for national use. If there are still a few who do not cherish themselves and are outside the group, and ultimately do evil, we can only proceed with the purpose of pacification and actively handle it, so that the people's pain can be relieved as soon as possible and the local area can be stabilized as soon as possible. All government construction plans can be realized as soon as possible. I hope that you will follow this main point, discuss it in depth, and follow the spirit of the leader of the committee, who is determined to overcome all difficulties, and to work hard, practically, and resolutely, so that you will not fail the trust of the central government and the expectations of the people." After the speech, the discussion of various proposals began, and the meeting adjourned at 12:00. Jiang Dingwen hosted a banquet at his private residence on Xianhou Street for the participants to gather. The second meeting continued at 2:00 pm and adjourned at 5:00 pm. The third meeting opened at 10:00 am on the 11th and adjourned at 12:00 pm. At noon, the officials of the Pacification Headquarters hosted a banquet for the attendees at the Ziyuan Hotel. The fourth meeting continued at 2:00 pm. Jiang Dingwen delivered the closing remarks and adjourned the meeting after taking a group photo.

Types of Proposals

A total of 67 proposals were passed at the two-day meeting, including 13 on reorganizing local teams and eliminating remnants of bandits, 10 on training the people and clearing the countryside and organizing the baojia system, 12 on building roads and adding telegraphs and telephones, 15 on pacifying refugees and handling local aftermath, 3 on promoting market prosperity and rescuing rural areas, 2 on promoting the New Life Movement, 4 on the powers and expenses of various pacification zones and their subordinate organizations, and 8 on military transportation.

Report to the Capital

After the meeting closed, Jiang Dingwen hosted a banquet at his private residence at 6:00 pm that evening to bid farewell to the attending commanders, division commanders, and representatives. The commanders and division commanders all returned to their defense posts on the 12th. Jiang originally planned to go to the capital in person to report everything, but since he could not make the trip, he decided to send Li Jianai, Chief of Staff of the Pacification Headquarters, as a representative to report to the central government and meet with Chairman Jiang to ask for instructions on everything. It is heard that Chief of Staff Li will take the plane north as soon as the proposals are sorted out.

Central Government Sends Commissioners to Songjiang to Investigate Land

Since the land survey work in Songjiang County began under the guidance of Wang Shaoyou, the special district investigator of the Land Committee, the work has been progressing smoothly, and the party and government sides have been cooperating effectively. In order to provide on-the-ground guidance, Wang has started the first phase of sampling inspections. Since the 10th, he has successively completed sampling inspections in Zhangze Tinglin Jinshanwei and Hua Yang Xinzhuang Fengjing Tianmashan districts in Punan and Pubei. Whenever Wang arrives at a place, he must first inquire in detail about the investigation process from the county investigators, review the completed forms, and give detailed instructions separately. Then, he immediately sets off with them for sampling inspections. His actions are extremely swift and his attitude is very amiable, so the people in all places can tell him the truth. The results of the sampling inspections are very good. Wang also believes that local party affairs, education, winter defense, and other undertakings are closely related to the revitalization of rural areas. Therefore, he has successively inspected the second district party headquarters and the first branch of the third district, visited Huayang Yandong Zhel Linwei City and other elementary schools, and the winter defense organizations in various places. He also gave a speech in Yandong. He also inquired in detail about the situation of the salt fields, the lives of the salt farmers, and the Zhelincheng, where the generals Yu Dayou and Qi Jiguang put down the Japanese pirates, and the Punans Academy, where the sage Gu Tinglin encouraged agriculture and lectures, and their anecdotes. It is heard that his impressions of this trip will be reported to the central government in detail.

Suzhou Requests Abolition of Vegetable Tax

The vegetable market tax inside and outside Suzhou City is contracted by Wei Du to the county government, and 300 yuan is paid monthly. The contractor also dispatches a large number of tax collectors to collect taxes from various vegetable vendors. Whether they are peddlers or stallholders, they must pay the tax. Therefore, the vegetable vendors believe that the tax is excessive and disruptive. They submitted a petition to the county government a few days ago requesting the cancellation of the business license. Yesterday (the 17th), more than a dozen people from the business community, including Pang Tiansheng, Song Youpei, and Cheng Ganqing, jointly submitted a petition to the civil and financial departments and the county government, stating that the contracting system had been abolished long ago. Furthermore, the vegetable tax in Suzhou only amounted to 300 yuan per month in the government's revenue, while the contractor arbitrarily imposed excessive taxes and harassed the vendors in every way. These small vendors are making a small profit and cannot bear the harassment. Furthermore, this vegetable tax is one of the excessive taxes and miscellaneous levies and should be abolished by order to reduce the burden on the small people.

Wuxi Yixing Liyang Refugees Sell Their Children

Last year's drought and insect plague were the worst in 60 years. Yixing and Liyang counties in Jiangsu Province were the most severely affected. Residents of the disaster areas fled outwards en masse. At this time of severe winter weather, they were suffering from hunger and cold, and their cries of grief were unbearable. Although charitable organizations in various places are raising funds for relief, they are unable to help because of the large number of people. According to a visitor from Houqiao, a suburb of Wuxi, dozens of refugees from Yixing and Liyang have arrived in the area recently, begging from farmers. At the end of their tether, they painfully sold 12 of their children, large and small, to others for only a dozen or twenty yuan each. However, it is difficult to determine whether they are criminals taking the opportunity to abduct children.

Suzhou Zhenjiang Continues to Catch Human Traffickers

The Supervisory Department of the County Public Security Bureau cracked down on a general organization for human trafficking in the southeast in Xiang'anli and other places a few days ago, and detained 10 male and female criminals. The details have been recorded in yesterday's newspaper. It is now learned that the Public Security Bureau dispatched inspectors Ge and Wu again that day, carrying documents to Suzhou and Zhenjiang, and together with the police officers of the respective counties, cracked down on a branch organization at No. 24 Xiqilin Lane in Suzhou, and arrested the main criminal, Meng Ruifu. They also continued to arrest a female criminal, Jin Xiangyun, at No. 1 Changanli, Xiaojie, Zhenjiang. They were separately escorted back to Wuxi yesterday for interrogation.

Major Fire at Northwest Corner of Nantong City at Midnight

A sudden fire broke out at twelve o'clock on the 15th at the northwest corner of Nantong City, where the shops were lined up. Fire brigades from all roads rushed to the rescue. It was extinguished at three o'clock on the morning of the 16th. It is estimated that 13 shops, including Datong Lumber Yard and Xiangxing Basin Bucket Shop, were burned down.

Method for Eliminating Smuggling Disputes

Due to the conflict between the anti-smuggling tax police in Tonghai area and the villagers when inspecting salt, the tax police district chief and the county magistrate are discussing ways to eliminate smuggling disputes. It has been decided that for cases reported that are not caught in the act, the reporter should obtain a counter-prosecution pledge from the officers of each team at any time, and the district chief will issue a warrant to allow execution, and temporarily notify the township head of the location to report the search with the reporter to prevent abuses.

Chairman Chiang Kai-shek Summoned Important Officials of the Municipal Government Yesterday

Second Batch of Silver Arrived in Shanghai from Hong Kong Today

Totaling 750,000 Yuan

The Rest Will Arrive Successively

According to Xinxin News Agency, in order to regulate domestic finance, the Foreign Exchange Stabilization Committee had the committee banks, Central Bank, Bank of China, and Bank of Communications purchase and transport a large amount of silver to Shanghai from Hong Kong to cope with the situation. The first batch of 500,400 yuan has already been transported to Shanghai a few days ago and deposited in the three banks. The second batch, totaling 750,000 yuan, has been loaded onto the President Taft of the Dale Company and the Empress of Russia of the Changxing Company and transported to Shanghai. It is expected that they will arrive at the port this afternoon, at which time the Central Bank and the Bank of Communications will carry out customs clearance procedures and then unload the silver ashore and store it in the warehouse. It is also heard that the third batch, about 500,000 yuan, will be loaded onto the President McKinley on the 21st and transported to Shanghai. The rest will arrive successively, and the city's finances will become more stable.

Zhejiang Province Public Bonds Mortgaged for 2 Million Yuan

Today's Discussion of Loan Contract

The Zhejiang Provincial Government, in urgent need of funds for various public works, disaster relief construction, and settlement of old debts, has decided to mortgage local public bonds with a face value of 10 million yuan from the 23rd year of the Republic of China to Shanghai banks for 6 million yuan at a 60% discount for application. It specially appointed Xu Qingfu, Director of the Department of Finance, to come to Shanghai to negotiate with various banks. After several days of negotiations in Shanghai, the banks considered that the end of the lunar year was approaching and it would be difficult to approve the full amount. It has now been decided to first borrow 2 million yuan, and the remaining 4 million yuan will be discussed after the lunar New Year. After the amount of the loan was determined, Xu decided to convene representatives of the borrowing banks, including China, Communications, Zhejiang Xingye, Zhejiang Industrial, China Industrial, Siming, Shanghai, Jin Cheng, Zhongnan, Yanyeh, Dalu, and Tongshang, today to discuss the draft mortgage loan contract in order to finalize and sign it as soon as possible.

The Municipal Federation Issued a Declaration of Market Relief Yesterday

Scheduled to Convene Industrial and Commercial Figures to Discuss Specific Measures

The Shanghai First Special District Citizens' Federation, considering the increasing decline of industry and commerce and the impending collapse of the Shanghai market, is seeking ways to provide relief as a matter of urgent importance. The representative assembly has resolved on a relief plan. In order to concentrate efforts and actively proceed, it has been decided to convene various industrial and commercial organizations in the city on January 21 to discuss effective overall relief measures to alleviate the difficulties faced by businesses. The details are as follows:

Scheduled Meeting

The Federation sent letters to various organizations yesterday, scheduling a general meeting on the 21st of this month. The original letter stated: "Dear Sirs, the decline of industry and commerce and the slump in the market in recent years are unprecedented in the history of Shanghai's commercial prosperity and decline. In view of this, the Federation has submitted the following resolutions to the Fourth Representative Assembly: (A) A one-year extension of the general closure of industry and commerce, with interest settled as usual, and a six-month extension of rent payments. We hereby record these resolutions and respectfully inform you. We have scheduled a general meeting of representatives from various industrial and commercial organizations in the city at the Municipal Chamber of Commerce at 2:00 PM on the 21st of this month to proceed together. The matter concerns the relief of the market situation, so we hope that you will send two representatives with a letter to attend and participate in order to gather diverse opinions and achieve greater benefits. Please do not delay."

Declaration Published

The Federation issued a declaration yesterday, stating: "The decline of the Shanghai market is a fact that is obvious to everyone and cannot be denied. All citizens with a vested interest should immediately take action to seek relief in order to avoid mutual destruction. Historically, Shanghai has been a base for economic aggression by various countries, and its collapse would be of little regret. However, if the Chinese people can utilize it properly, it can be transformed into a key to expanding foreign trade, reversing the trade deficit, and turning it into a trade surplus. Some attribute the decline of the Shanghai market to the resistance against Japan on January 28. In fact, the Shanghai market was able to survive until this year before showing an even greater decline, which was due to the benefits of the January 28 incident. Before January 28, the frenzy of speculation in Shanghai's real estate was like the scorching sun at midday. There were countless instances of raising rents, forcing evictions, and rebuilding to benefit oneself at the expense of others, so that citizens had to reduce other essential needs in order to meet the insatiable demands of real estate speculators. After the January 28 incident, this trend subsided slightly, and the rent reduction movement was able to begin. Otherwise, the continued increase in rents would not have stopped. Therefore, the primary factor contributing to the decline of the Shanghai market was real estate speculation. The second factor was the years of famine and banditry in the interior, which led to the disappearance of purchasing power in rural areas, resulting in the stagnation of Shanghai goods. The third factor was the lack of sales channels for industry and commerce, so businesses used stages, extensive advertising, and erected electric light arches to attract customers. One store did this, and then a hundred stores did this. One industry did this, and then a hundred industries did this. Business remained the same, but expenses increased. However, outsiders and real estate speculators still claimed that stores were crowded with customers and business was booming. In reality, those standing there were listening to the radio, watching discount advertisements, and admiring the electric light signs. It was just people watching people. There were no real customers. The Federation convened a representative assembly on January 16 to discuss in detail how to relieve the depression in the Shanghai market and the decline of industry and commerce. The assembly unanimously resolved: (A) To extend the general closure of industry and commerce for one year, with interest settled as usual. (1) To issue a declaration. (2) To petition the party and government organs to issue a clear order of approval. (3) To send letters to the National Federation of Chambers of Commerce, the Shanghai Chamber of Commerce, and various industrial and commercial organizations to proceed together. (B) To petition the Executive Yuan to instruct the Ministry of Finance to allocate loans from the Central Bank to relieve industry and commerce in Shanghai. (C) (1) To petition the municipal government and send letters to the Municipal Council to collect property taxes on vacant houses. (2) To petition the competent authorities to issue a clear order postponing rent payments for six months. (3) To petition the municipal government and send letters to the Chinese Ratepayers' Association to reduce rents. All of the above are merely the minimum measures required by the facts. Some may think that extending the general closure is too extraordinary and useless. It should be noted that distant examples include the postponement of American war bonds and German domestic debt, which were both clear and decisive actions taken by great statesmen in power. A recent example is the extension of the general closure in Shanghai after the January 28 incident, which was due to the efforts of Mr. Wang Xiaolai, Chairman of the Municipal Chamber of Commerce at the time. Anyone in the market who is capable and active will be able to recognize the needs of the situation and express them to respond to extraordinary circumstances. If the above-mentioned measures are delayed, industry and commerce will disappear without a trace, and real estate will not only "sell for 70% off without a buyer or be mortgaged for 50% off." Under the circumstances where lenders only take in and do not release, it will also become worthless. What can be done with all businesses among the overflowing ranks of the unemployed? As for industry and commerce themselves, (1) those that can be merged should be merged, and those that can form business associations should do so. As the number of vacant houses in the market increases, it can reduce rents and encourage real estate speculators to return to their provinces, thereby lowering rents. (2) Minimize the use of electric lights, billboards, telephones, etc., and promote business methods to reduce expenses. If each store does this, the total amount of business will not increase. It will only increase expenses, increase costs, and make it more difficult to sell goods, thereby accelerating the rate of bankruptcy. If we can overcome this difficulty, and the interior improves next spring, purchasing power will recover, and goods will move, then we will enter a path of prosperity. Who can say for sure that this will not happen? It is precisely for the purpose of treating a serious illness quickly and then gradually recuperating and recovering. We also hope that municipal leaders like Yu Qiaqing will follow the example of 1927 and re-establish the Commercial Federation to respond to this extraordinary period in the market. This matter concerns the prosperity and decline of the Shanghai market. This declaration is hereby made for your public consideration. Shanghai First Special District Citizens' Federation, January 17, 1935."

The Emergency Relief and Universal Donation Association Resolved to Continue Fundraising

Donated Funds to be Used for Both Bandit and Drought Disaster Relief

The Emergency Relief and Universal Donation Association held a meeting in the Municipal Government Conference Room at 11:00 AM yesterday. The attendees included Pan Xusheng from the Municipal Chamber of Commerce, Wang Xiaolai from the Ratepayers' Association, Zhu Boyuan from the Municipal Chamber of Commerce, Long Peiyun from the Municipal General Labor Union, Huang Hanzhi from the China Foreign Famine Relief Committee, Guan Jiongzhi from the Chinese Red Cross Society, Wang Zhen from the Federation of Charitable Organizations, Du Yuesheng from the Local Self-Government Association, Qu Wenliu from the Various Provinces' Drought Relief Association, Xie Yanbo from the Boy Scout Council, Lin Meiyan from the Municipal Party Headquarters, and Wu Tiecheng, Yu Hongjun, and Li Dachao from the Municipal Government. Mayor Wu presided over the meeting, and Li Dachao served as the secretary. After formal greetings, the chairman reported that the total amount of donations received since the start of the universal donation campaign up to the 15th was over 86,000 yuan in foreign currency. The association is a support team for the Various Provinces' Drought Relief Association and intends to continue its efforts after the lunar New Year. Qu Wenliu also reported on the allocation of disaster relief donations to various provinces by the Various Provinces' Drought Relief Association (details omitted). The following matters were discussed: 1. To continue fundraising. 2. The principle of using donated funds for both bandit and drought disaster relief will be given equal importance. 3. All universal donations should be handed over to the Various Provinces' Drought Relief Association for management, but the universal donation funds should be primarily used for work-for-relief programs that benefit the disaster areas. 4. All requests for disaster relief should be forwarded to the Various Provinces' Drought Relief Association for processing.

The association is actively working on donations from the wealthy and is adopting effective measures to reach a strong resolution so that all wealthy individuals in the city can donate to help the disaster victims. The association also received the following donations yesterday: Yarn Industry Association, 100 foreign dollars; National Bank, 88.60 yuan in large silver dollars and 50 cents in small silver dollars; Meiwen Electric Silk Weaving Factory, 73.40 yuan in large silver dollars; East Asia Hotel, 27.80 yuan in large silver dollars and 78 cents in small silver dollars; Chengdong Elementary School, 5.20 yuan in large silver dollars and 78 cents in small silver dollars, and 6 copper coins; Songchun Elementary School, 7 yuan in large silver dollars and 52 cents in small silver dollars, and 23 copper coins; Minguang School, 42 cents in small silver dollars; Maicun Elementary School, 1 yuan in large silver dollars and 46 cents in small silver dollars; Qiming Girls' Middle School, 50 yuan in large silver dollars; Qiming Girls' Elementary School, 42 yuan in large silver dollars; Dagong Elementary School, 5 yuan in large silver dollars and 174 cents in small silver dollars, and 376 copper coins.

Suma Arrived in Shanghai Yesterday Afternoon

Visited the Japanese Ambassador to Report Everything, Scheduled to Enter Beijing Within Days

According to the Central News Agency, Suma, the Japanese Consul General in Beijing, was summoned back to his country last year to report everything to the Japanese Ministry of Foreign Affairs. Having completed his report, he toured various ports such as Pingjin and arrived in Shanghai yesterday afternoon at 2:00 PM on the Dalian Steamship Company's Fengtian Maru from Qingdao, which docked at the Huishan Wharf. His friends in Shanghai welcomed him at the port. After disembarking, he went to the Japanese Consulate General to meet with Japanese Ambassador Arimasa Akira and reported on his return to Japan. He is scheduled to leave Shanghai for Beijing within one or two days to assume his duties.

Consular Body Selects Consuls for the Year

Mr. Cunningham, the American Consul General and leader of the consular body in Shanghai, recently informed the Municipal Council that the American, British, and Japanese Consuls General have been publicly elected as the Consuls for the Year for the consular body, and Mr. Lange will continue to serve as the secretary. His correspondence address is the American Consulate General.

The leading consul also notified the Municipal Council that the consular body has designated the Dutch, Swiss, and Swedish Consuls General to serve as directors of the Public Hospital for this year. In the event of an absence, their respective acting Consuls General will take their place.

In addition, according to consular practice, three prison inspectors are elected each year to form an inspection committee. The acting Polish Consul General (Chairman), the German Vice Consul, and the British Consul have been selected to serve. The secretary of the committee will be the secretary of the consular body.

River Waters Recede, Few Ships

The water level in the Sichuan River has been receding sharply in recent days, and shipping has also declined. The transportation of goods from Shanghai to Sichuan has completely stopped, and the number of ships has been greatly reduced. The situation is described in detail below:

Great Reduction in Chinese Ships

In recent years, various small Chinese steamship companies operating on the Shanghai-Sichuan River route have suffered from business depression and price drops and have closed down one after another. However, the number of ships of the Minsheng Company has increased. Most of the ships of small companies have been merged into the Minsheng Company. Therefore, Minsheng Company has the greatest influence on the Shanghai-Chongqing, Yichang-Chongqing, and inland ships. Recently, troops are being transferred to Sichuan to suppress the communists. There is a need for commercial ships to be used for military purposes in the Sichuan River. Many Chinese commercial ships have been requisitioned, resulting in a great reduction in Chinese ships on the Shanghai-Chongqing and Yichang-Chongqing routes in recent days, a decrease of three-quarters compared to normal. Foreign commercial ships have also switched to smaller, shallow-draft vessels due to the low water level.

Suspension of Passenger and Freight Services

Two weeks ago, the exchange rate for Sichuan currency in Shanghai rose to 1,700 yuan. Although it has fallen slightly recently, it is still around 1,500 yuan. Due to the exchange rate, it is extremely uneconomical to send goods from Shanghai. For example, goods that cost one yuan in Shanghai cost two yuan in Sichuan. Passengers have been affected by this, and the transportation of goods from Shanghai to Sichuan has been temporarily suspended. Recently, due to the suppression of the communists and the approach of the lunar New Year, the transportation of goods to Sichuan has been affected by the inability to turn over funds in time, so people have stopped purchasing goods. According to people in the Sichuan business community, goods will not be available for loading until after the Lantern Festival (15th day of the first lunar month).

Two Important Telegrams from the All-Zhejiang Association Regarding Drought Relief

Seed Grain Should be Purchased in the Same County or Neighboring County to Suit the Soil

Water Conservancy Projects Should Focus on Local Tributaries and Small Rivers

Purchase and Distribution of Seed Grain

To Chairman Huang of the Zhejiang Provincial Government: The drought last summer was too severe, and in the severely affected areas, the rice crops failed completely. Those that had some harvest had dry and shriveled rice grains that could not be stored as seeds. Now that winter has arrived, the disaster-stricken farmers are facing starvation and freezing. It is not easy for them to even feed themselves, let alone have the resources to purchase seed grain. Spring plowing is approaching, and the spring planting season is about to begin. If seed grain is not provided for them, the farmers will be unable to plant, and the fertile fields will become barren. This will lead to continuous crop failures. It is important to seize the opportunity during this winter season to purchase the grain. If this is delayed, the grain will be milled into rice and stones, making it difficult to purchase. Please instruct the Relief Commission to quickly purchase and store a large amount of seed grain and send letters to the county governments to instruct the district townships to distribute the grain to the extremely poor farmers after verifying their identities. If there are concerns about insufficient funds, please allocate funds from the one million yuan of relief funds for this purpose. As there are differences in soil suitability for seed grain, the seed grain distributed to a particular county should be purchased from a nearby area with suitable soil to ensure growth. This matter concerns the preparation for disaster relief and should not be treated as a slow matter. Therefore, we are sending this telegram for your consideration and implementation. It would be in the public interest. The Shanghai All-Zhejiang Association, sincerely.

Expediting the Repair of Water Conservancy Projects

To Chairman Huang of the Zhejiang Provincial Government: The 20 million yuan of Zhejiang Province public bonds, approved by the Legislative Yuan, will be mostly used for public works. Since Committee Chairman Chiang issued the telegraphed announcement, the public works project has gained increasing attention. Zhejiang is an agricultural area, and agricultural water conservancy is of paramount importance for production and construction. Our association paid attention to the repair of water conservancy projects and the dredging of large and small rivers at the beginning of the drought last summer. Even now, after reflecting on the pain, it is not too late to mend the fold. The main rivers and ponds are related to transportation and water conservancy in one or several counties, requiring large-scale construction and huge costs. We should wait until a definitive plan is established before seeking large funds for dredging. However, tributaries and small rivers have been neglected by people, but their benefits for irrigating fields are significant. During this drought, areas near the ponds were able to have some harvest, while areas far from the ponds had severe reductions in harvests, even complete failure, due to shallow and blocked rivers, obstructed water sources, and difficult water lifting. Therefore, dredging local tributaries and small rivers is the most urgent priority for water conservancy. Now that we are preparing for public works, we should take advantage of the low water level in winter and the slack farming season to order all counties to organize and implement them simultaneously. In this severe winter, people are suffering from cold and starvation, and are crying out for food. Winter relief has not been widespread, and public works should not be delayed. There are also concerns that the spring floods will rise, and the farming season will begin, making the work difficult and interfering with farming. The public works project may be suspended, and the starving people will be left to die in ditches. Therefore, we are sending this telegram for your consideration and implementation. The Shanghai All-Zhejiang Association, sincerely.

First Italian Ambassador to China, Vincenzo Arangio Ruiz, Scheduled to Present Credentials

Arriving in Beijing on the 23rd Evening, Meeting Chairman Lin on the 25th

Railway Bureau Prepared a Special Train; His Wife and Others Traveling with Him

Vincenzo Arangio Ruiz, the newly appointed first Italian Ambassador to China, arrived in Shanghai some days ago to assume his duties. It has been learned that after Mr. Ruiz sent a copy of his credentials to Beijing, Chairman Lin scheduled a meeting at the Presidential Office on the morning of the 25th at 11:00 AM. The Ministry of Foreign Affairs was instructed to notify the Italian Embassy's Beijing office, which then telegraphed Shanghai. Yesterday morning, according to Mr. Ross, the First Secretary of Chinese Affairs at the Italian Embassy, Ambassador Ruiz, upon receiving the news, decided to travel to Beijing with his wife and others on the evening of the 23rd so that they could arrive in Beijing on the morning of the 24th and pay their respects to President Wang first.

Traveling Staff

In addition to his wife, Mr. Ruiz will be accompanied by Mr. Gabsiewicz, First Secretary; Mr. Sciadai Dini, Second Secretary; Mr. Ross, First Secretary of Chinese Affairs; Mr. Fraiulo, Second Secretary of Chinese Affairs; Mr. Spaco, Naval Attaché; Mr. Delago, Air Attaché; and others.

Railway Bureau to Prepare a Special Train

It has also been learned that when Chairman Lin meets with the Italian Ambassador, the ceremony will be grand and in accordance with diplomatic protocol. The Ministry of Foreign Affairs will first send Mr. Lin Tongshi, the head of the Protocol Department, to Shanghai on the 23rd to welcome and escort Mr. Ruiz to Beijing. The Shanghai office of the Ministry of Foreign Affairs has sent a letter to the Railway Bureau to prepare a special train car for Mr. Ruiz's use.

Joint Petition to the Central Government by Five Exchanges to Request Exemption from Exchange Tax

Narrating Business Difficulties and Requesting Postponement

Issuing a Joint Declaration and Seeking Assistance from the Chamber of Commerce

The Da Gong News Agency reports that the Ministry of Finance has decided to start collecting exchange tax from February 1st. The gold industry and other five exchanges in this city, burdened by the increased cost and its impact on business, have unanimously resolved to strive against it. Yesterday, they sent a special telegram to the central government requesting exemption and issued a joint declaration, also sending a letter to the city's Chamber of Commerce for assistance. The contents of the telegrams are transcribed below:

Telegram to the Central Government

Respectfully submitted to Chairman Lin of the National Government, Chairman Jiang of the Military Affairs Commission, President Wang of the Executive Yuan, President Sun of the Legislative Yuan, Minister Kong of the Ministry of Finance, and Minister Chen of the Ministry of Industry: We, the associations, previously heard of the proposed collection of transaction tax by the esteemed Yuan and Ministry and submitted a petition, laying out the merchants' difficult business situation. Now reading in the newspaper that the tax item will be submitted to the Legislative Yuan for review, we are deeply alarmed. Taxation is the duty of the citizens, and the merchants of our associations dare not lag behind. However, with the current market depression, financial exhaustion, and national industry and commerce on the verge of bankruptcy, it is truly impossible to bear. We must again present to the esteemed Yuan and Ministry the actual situation of our associations' business difficulties, as well as the interests of the entire economy. Throughout the years, our country has suffered from internal and external troubles, and the recent water and drought disasters have further aggravated the situation. The people's vitality has been greatly damaged. Coupled with the economic aggression of European and American powers, as well as our eastern neighbor, the outflow of silver, the decline in prices, the closure of shops, the unemployment of workers, the bankruptcy of rural areas, and the decline of cities are all recorded in newspapers. All these phenomena indicate the shaking of the entire economy and the hidden crisis of the future. Although our government has made every effort to manage and provide relief, due to the deep weakness, like a long-ill person, it is difficult to recover even with daily ginseng. Therefore, although prevention work is thorough, the severe situation has not diminished. At this critical moment, the national industry and commerce are all breathing their last, struggling to survive. The merchants of our associations are in the same situation. How can they be an exception? If transaction tax is levied again, burdening the entrustees, it would be no different from strangling a dying person. Moreover, the adverse effects will not only affect the business of our associations, pushing them into a dead end with no way to survive, but also directly eliminate the function of the exchange in the economic sphere, leading to a de facto standstill. Indirectly, it would be tantamount to a fatal blow to the entire industry and commerce of our country. Furthermore, after the stagnation of the exchange, foreigners will inevitably have the opportunity to control our industry and commerce. The activity of foreign merchants' exchanges in the past may even resume today. In that case, the effect of taxation will not be seen, and the economic crisis will break out. What could be more urgent than this? As a result, the government's goal of collecting new taxes may not be achieved, and the original business tax revenue will also disappear. This is not what our government initially expected, nor is it the intention to cherish industry and commerce. Our associations dare not deliberately make alarmist remarks to sensationalize. We do so because of a sense of impending danger and cannot remain silent. Therefore, we respectfully submit another telegram explaining the reasons why we cannot bear the transaction tax, earnestly requesting the esteemed Yuan and Ministry to discern the subtle points and approve the postponement of the tax bill to cultivate the national strength and maintain the overall situation. This would be a great virtue. We await your orders with extreme anxiety and fear. Respectfully submitted, Shanghai Chinese Cotton Cloth Exchange Brokers Association Representative Bian Futang, Shanghai Chinese Securities Exchange Brokers Association Representative Wang Zhengruo, Shanghai Gold Exchange Brokers Association Representative Zhan Liansheng, Shanghai Flour Exchange Brokers Association Representative Zhang Weiyun, Shanghai Grain Exchange Brokers Association Representative Xue Chengzhang, together with reverence, Xiao Yin.

Letter to the City Chamber of Commerce

Respected Sirs, the establishment of formal exchanges in our country began after 1918. After the turmoil of the 1920s, the foundation gradually became solid. After more than ten years of painstaking management, it has become the current situation, fulfilling its functions of forming prices, transferring risks, and circulating materials. Now, our government is collecting transaction tax on exchanges. The issue is not whether the legal intention is correct. In fact, under the current situation of the business community in our country today, the implementation of transaction tax must take into account the associated malpractices. Once transaction tax is collected, if brokers, for their own benefit, do not pass on the burden to the entrustees but raise the commission fee for trading, they will only endure the burden for a while and maintain the original commission rate. The malpractices above are all very serious. For example, if the commission fee for trading is raised, the direct result will inevitably affect the reduction of all transactions. The exchange will inevitably fall into a state of stagnation because of this, which will inevitably make the depressed business situation more dull, and the stagnant materials will be more difficult to activate. Then the business tax originally paid by the exchange based on profit will also be greatly reduced, which will harm the income of the national treasury. This is a matter of concern. If transaction tax is also collected on the trading of public bonds (exempt in Japan), the result in the future will inevitably lead to the stagnation of old debts, and it will be even more difficult to issue new debts. This is a matter of concern. If there is more hindrance to exchange trading, there will be more difficulty in the transfer of enterprise stocks. Thus, established enterprises will be difficult to develop, and unborn enterprises will be difficult to produce. This is a matter of concern. The loss of brokers will inevitably affect the survival of the exchange over time. Unfortunately, if foreign exchanges that are not subject to our legal control take the opportunity to revive and deliberately disrupt the market, then our country's exchanges will inevitably have to shut down completely, and the prices of our country's goods will not be able to but listen to foreigners. The exchanges that have been fought for over the past ten years will be handed over to others. This is a matter of concern. Therefore, in terms of today's facts, in order to save the depressed business situation, the transaction tax should be temporarily suspended. In recent years, the world economic panic has invaded from the outside, and the scourge of water, drought, bandits, and chaos has besieged from the inside. The phenomenon of rural bankruptcy and fleeing famine has increased day by day. Industry and commerce have declined, and the circulation of materials has become more difficult. China's entire economic activity is deteriorating, and the future crisis is appalling. The economy is so sluggish that its representation in the exchanges is the gradual decline of transactions. Moreover, recently, the financial market in Shanghai has experienced sudden changes from time to time. People are panicked and cannot live in peace. At the end of the lunar year, the number of companies declared closed by the industrial and commercial sectors can be seen in newspapers every day. The end of the lunar year is approaching again. Since the Ministry of Finance's proposal to collect transaction tax, people have panicked, and all transactions have suddenly shrunk. If the transaction tax is collected at this time, the depressed business situation may become increasingly depressed, and the devastated economy will be transformed into panic. If unfortunately it comes to this, the effectiveness of taxation will not be seen, and the economic crisis has already begun, which is contrary to the original intention of taxation. In order to alleviate the current economic crisis and stabilize people's hearts, the transaction tax really needs to be temporarily suspended. Furthermore, the current transaction tax was promulgated in 1927, but it was not implemented because the tax rate at that time was lower than the current tax rate, and the business situation at that time was more prosperous than the current business situation. At that time, it was not implemented due to the request of our associations. Today, the situation of the industrial and commercial sectors is far worse than that at that time. The distance between the two cannot be calculated by miles, and the tax rate has been increased. Moreover, the tax rate proposed by the Ministry of Finance this time seems to be based on one-tenth of the gross commission of the exchange and brokers for the calculation of goods. However, the collection of stamp tax is particularly high. The following table can be used as proof:

Item Category Ministry of Finance Tax Rate Exchange and Broker Gross Commission Ratio

Stamp Tax (per item) 1 jiao 8.41 times and 2

Cotton (per 100 dan) 9 jiao 9 yuan 1/10

Cotton Yarn (per 100 bales) 3.5 yuan 35 yuan 1/10

Flour (per 1000 bags) 7 jiao 7 yuan 1/10

Wheat, Grains, Yellow Beans, Red Beans (per cart) 1.4 yuan 14 yuan 1/10

Soybean Cake (per 1000 jin) 7 jiao 7 yuan 1/10

Soybean Oil (per 100 dan) 7 jiao 7 yuan 1/10

In terms of the ratio of the above tax rates, the stamp tax rate is more than twice that of the gross commission of the exchange and brokers, which is really unreasonable. For example, in terms of valuation of various grains, the tax rate is as high as 6 or 7 ten-thousandths, which is higher than other goods, and is unfair. It is also easier to make the shaky financial market more depressed. In 1927, it was not implemented due to various relationships. Today, in order to maintain the depression of commerce and take care of the difficulties of merchants, the transaction tax should be temporarily suspended. In short, today's collection of transaction tax still has great difficulties in implementation. If it is forcibly implemented, the effectiveness cannot be foreseen, and the danger is imminent. The above-mentioned matters have long been understood by your association. We have always admired your association for protecting the interests of merchants and making every effort. We hereby earnestly request your association to uphold justice and quickly forward it to the Executive Yuan, the Legislative Yuan, and the Ministry of Finance to revoke the original case of collecting transaction tax in order to maintain the overall situation and relieve merchants' difficulties. We are extremely grateful. This is addressed to the Shanghai Chamber of Commerce, Cotton Cloth Exchange Mu Ouchu, Flour Exchange Wang Yiting, Gold Industry Exchange Xu Fenghui, Grain Exchange Gu Xinyi, Securities Exchange Zhang Weiru, Cotton Cloth Brokers Association Bian Futang, Securities Brokers Association Wang Zhengru, Flour Brokers Association Zhang Weiyun, Gold Industry Brokers Association Zhan Liansheng, Grain Brokers Association Xue Chengzhang, jointly initiated.

Joint Declaration

The Shanghai Cotton Cloth, Flour, Gold Industry, Securities, and Grain Exchange Brokers Association declares a request for the temporary suspension of the collection of transaction tax. In recent years, the world economic panic has invaded from the outside, and the scourge of water, drought, bandits, and chaos has besieged from the inside. As a result, the phenomenon of rural bankruptcy and fleeing famine has increased day by day. Industry and commerce have declined, and the circulation of materials has become more difficult. China's entire economic activity is deteriorating, and the future crisis is appalling. The economy is so sluggish that its representation in the exchanges is the gradual decline of transactions. If we take the number of flour transactions as an example, it reached about 300 million bags in 1931, and it decreased to 100 million bags in 1932. In 1933, it was less than 100 million bags. In the past three years, it has gradually decreased by two-thirds. In terms of the gold industry, the number of transactions this year is only half of that in 1930. The trading of securities, cotton, and grain is also in the same situation, tending to decline. The business of merchants depends entirely on the amount of transactions. Therefore, the large reduction in the amount of transactions can also indirectly indicate the decline in the business of merchants. (The content of the middle paragraph of the joint declaration is the same as the meaning of the letter to the city chamber of commerce, and the full text is published on the front page of various newspapers, so it is omitted). In short, today's collection of transaction tax still has great difficulties in implementation. If it is forcibly implemented, the effectiveness cannot be foreseen, and the danger is imminent. Our associations are in it, and the feelings are real. We dare not remain silent because of the danger. In addition to submitting separate requests to the Central Political Council, the National Government, the Executive Yuan, the Legislative Yuan, and the Ministry of Finance, we will publish the reasons for the request to the society. In order to save the current economic crisis, we hope that the national industrial and commercial sectors will rise up to assist and advocate together. Then the industrial and commercial sectors will be fortunate, and the society will be fortunate. We hereby declare.

Shi Shouyu Talks About the Situation of Overseas Chinese in Celebes Island

Mr. Shi Shouyu, a Fujianese overseas Chinese businessman from Celebes Island, Dutch East Indies, returned to China this time to investigate the industry. He arrived in Shanghai from Hong Kong yesterday and stayed at the New Asia Hotel. A reporter from the Guowen News Agency, introduced by Mr. Liu Shimu, went to interview him and inquired about the situation of the islands in Southeast Asia. According to him, the commercial situation in the various parts of Southeast Asia has been declining day by day, and the export of goods has been decreasing day by day. If there is no turning point in a few days, the tragic situation cannot be described in words. Moreover, the situation in the Dutch East Indies is even more dangerous after the failure of the Japanese-Dutch commercial conference. In order to protect their own interests, countries have raised tariffs, making it difficult for foreign goods to enter. For example, the major commodities produced in Celebes Island, such as trepang, coconut, rattan, resin (industrial supplies translated as dianmatou), etc., are all important local products, but there is no market. The natives are bloodless and exhausted, and the resident government is exacting various taxes. The Chinese Ma Yao Tang Longfei family in this island has been taxed by the resident government as much as 200,000 guilders (about 400,000 yuan in national currency) in the past two years. Other families can be inferred. Middle-class families can barely cope, and ordinary families often sell all their property to pay the heavy tax. The incidents of our resident overseas Chinese being robbed and killed by natives in rural areas are often heard. If they move to cities to run businesses, those with weak capital often find that their income cannot offset the heavy taxes of the government, and the result is bankruptcy. Alas, how difficult is the current situation of our overseas Chinese! Many overseas Chinese now want to take the remaining assets and return to their home country to run businesses, but soldiers and bandits are everywhere in the two provinces of Fujian and Guangdong, and there is almost no clean land to live in. Now, overseas Chinese hope that the government of their home country will have a relief plan. I have returned to China this time to investigate the industries in the country in which overseas Chinese can invest, and I plan to report to overseas in the future. I plan to stay in Shanghai for a week and go to the Yangtze River and other places.

Statistics on Syphilis Tests for Wet Nurses at the Health Testing Institute

Also Tested for Tuberculosis and Trachoma Infectivity in Breast Milk

The Shanghai Health Bureau's Health Testing Institute, in view of the fact that wet nurses suffering from hidden diseases have a great impact on the health of infants, previously notified the citizens who employ wet nurses to send them to the institute for blood tests for syphilis. The results of the tests in the past four months are as follows: in September, a total of 60 people were tested, and 6 people were found to have syphilis. In October, a total of 74 people were tested, and 17 people were found to have syphilis. In November, a total of 58 people were tested, and 15 people were found to have syphilis. In December, a total of 65 people were tested, and 21 people were found to have syphilis. In total, 257 wet nurses were tested in the four months, and 59 people were found to have syphilis, accounting for almost more than a quarter. For the safety of infants, all wet nurses who are sent to the institute for blood tests for syphilis can also be tested by the institute for tuberculosis, trachoma, infectivity, skin diseases, and the chemical composition of breast milk at the same time. The fee for each person is 5 yuan, including the blood test.

Flower Powder Industry Guild Discusses Trademark Name Issues

Because it does not conflict with the central government's interpretation

Requesting the Bureau of Social Affairs to approve registration

Chinese social customs often lead to identical store names. This system violates current trends. Recently, the Municipal Chamber of Commerce received instructions from the Executive Yuan, based on Judicial Yuan Interpretation No. 1140 regarding Article 19 of the General Principles for Merchants, stating that within the same city or town, no one may imitate a previously registered trademark to operate the same business, limited to the same city or town. A notice was issued to all trade associations to comply. The Shanghai Flower Powder Industry Guild, because flower powder shops have traditionally used the name "Dai Chunlin" for fifty to sixty years, believes this interpretation will inevitably cause disputes. A meeting of the executive committee was held yesterday at 2:00 PM at the guild's location on Guanyi Street in the city. Xu Furu presided, and Sheng Shiwei recorded the meeting. The chairman reported that the interpretation was related to the "Dai Chunlin" trademark, which our industry has used for decades. Dozens of businesses have registered with the Bureau of Social Affairs simultaneously, but only one has been approved. If this interpretation is mistakenly used as an example, dozens of "Dai Chunlin" trademark businesses will be affected. A public discussion was requested to avoid disputes. Standing committee member Zhao Guohua stated that the interpretation does not apply to our industry. Our industry has used the name "Dai Chunlin" for a long time without registration, so it does not conflict with the interpretation. It was resolved that Xu Furu, Yang Housheng, and Cheng Guichu, three committee members, would explain the situation to the Bureau of Social Affairs and request approval.

Huangpu River to Have High Tide Next Month on the 4th

Also high tide the day after, on the Start of Spring Festival

Roads in particularly low-lying areas may see water

According to the Datong News Agency, the fourth day of next month is the Lunar New Year's Day. The next day is the Start of Spring Festival. According to predictions by the Shanghai Dredging Bureau, there will be a high tide in the Huangpu River on these two days. The lunar New Year's Day high tide is predicted to start at 11:49 AM, and at 12:44 PM, the tide is predicted to increase, and the flow rate will be 2.0 nautical miles per hour. By 1:19 PM, the tide will reach its highest point, at 10 feet, 6 inches, and 4 points. The next day (February 5) is the Start of Spring Festival and there will also be a high tide. The high tide will start at 11:39 AM, and at 1:21 PM, the flow will increase and reach 2.2 nautical miles per hour. By 1:57 PM, the tide will reach its highest point, at 10 feet, 1 inch, and 8 points. If there is wind on these days, the tide may flood roads in the city's low-lying areas through the sewers.
