Spring and Autumn

Little Western Paradise

— Written by Zhang Henshui

Chapter 7: Hearing Words, She Hides Her Tears and Sells Herself to Tell of Hardship; Cautiously Observing, He Asks to Rely on the East with Earnest Affection

"So then, let us proceed with the second step of our plan, to actually seek an audience ourselves. With this spirit and following these steps, I believe we can achieve our goal. To be honest, no matter how high-ranking an official, they are most afraid of us not being able to see their face. If we can see their face, and use the method of encirclement to surround them, we need not fear that they will not give us a position. The difficulty lies in this hurdle of meeting, which is not easily overcome." As he spoke, he raised his hands and shook his head repeatedly, as if to say that he felt somewhat unappreciated for his talents. Li Shilian thought to himself, "The more you say this makes sense, the more I cannot let you get to know Cheng Zhiqian. Otherwise, I would be giving away such a good opportunity to you." So he smiled and said, "What you say might not be correct. However, this Cheng is also extremely shrewd and a bit arrogant, probably not easy to deal with. I don't want to bother with him." Zhang Jiefu snorted in his nose and laughed, "What's the big deal?" When Li Shilian heard him say that he had his own methods, he felt even more displeased, and said faintly, "Then we'll see if there's an opportunity. I'm too lazy to be friends with people of such low status and high temper." Zhang Jiefu's level of experience in society was above that of Li Shilian. How could he not know Li Shilian's unhappy attitude? Following that, he smiled and did not continue the conversation. He let Li Shilian leave, and himself hurried out of the hotel, only returning after about an hour. He saw that Cheng Zhiqian was still in his room and had not gone out. Without even entering his own room, he stood at the door and bowed slightly, saying with a smile, "Mr. Cheng hasn't gone out yet?" Zhiqian said, "Please come in and sit." Zhang Jiefu could not have wished for that more, and immediately walked in. But there was one thing that immediately caught his attention: on the table was a card with eight lines written on it, saying, "Tomorrow at 11:00 AM, please grace me with your presence at the Dalu Spring for a simple meal. Please do not decline. Your humble younger brother, Li Shilian, bows." This was truly a case of "Do not say you travel early, there are those who travel even earlier." However, on Zhang Jiefu's side, the approach would be different. (115)

Discussion of National Painting

— Yi Mei

Looking through the history of Chinese painting, it can be said that talent has emerged in abundance. Every era has had several representative works, such as Wu Daozi's Tang paintings, Ma Yuan's Song paintings, Ni Yunlin's Yuan paintings, and Shen Zhou, Tang Yin, Wen Zhengming, and Qiu Ying's Ming paintings, as well as the Four Wangs, Wu Li, and Yun Shouping's Qing paintings. Each has its own style and spirit, so it is no wonder that they can be remembered for a long time as masters of art. Reaching the present day, although shaken by the Western trends, some people have worked hard in the areas of oil painting, charcoal drawing, and watercolor painting, but there are also not a few who are steadfast in their principles and purely pursue Chinese painting. Especially in Shanghai, national painters often hold national painting exhibitions, both collaborative and individual. Although superficially, these exhibitions are meant to give people an understanding and appreciation of national painting, in reality, they are mostly due to supply exceeding demand, with no patrons for the works. Therefore, they have no choice but to hold exhibitions here and there, selling paintings and offering framing, and engaging in major publicity. As a result, they often gain very little and instead lose money on expenses and advertising fees. As a result, the future of national painting seems to be covered by a gray curtain, with no light to be seen. Some say that painting and calligraphy are luxuries for the wealthy. Since the market is not prosperous and the countryside is bankrupt, people are struggling to make a living, so where would they have spare money to buy paintings and calligraphy to hang up? This is certainly very reasonable, but on closer thought, there are other reasons. In the past, people used paintings to represent personality. Entering a room with famous artists' transcendent works on all four walls, one could imagine the elegant and refined character of the owner. Moreover, when carrying a folding fan with the signature of a famous painter, others would know that you were a person of great importance and would not dare to deceive or humiliate you, saving you much trouble. Nowadays, the social atmosphere has changed drastically, with money being the prerequisite everywhere. There is no talk of personality, let alone any distinction between elegance and vulgarity, so naturally there is no need to use paintings to represent anything. Furthermore, paintings are used as decorations. Now, houses are trending towards Westernization. Hanging a Chinese painting in a Westernized house seems out of place. Especially recently, all architecture and arrangements have favored the Cubist style, with simplicity and cleanliness being considered beautiful, a complete reversal of the previous elaborate decorations, so paintings are naturally relegated to the list of things to be eliminated. Therefore, judging from this trend, national painting is getting worse and worse and has reached its end. I fear that there will be no more days of flourishing and great development. I know a very famous old painter. Once, a young man admired his wonderful painting skills and asked someone to introduce him, wishing to become his disciple. The old painter asked the introducer: "Does this young man have any assets at home? What are his expectations for the future after he learns?" The introducer said: "His family is poor and he plans to make a living by painting." The old painter replied very bluntly, "In that case, it is better to advise the young man to learn some other business that has more hope. If he follows me, he will inevitably starve to death in the future. Don't delay his future." How painful were the old painter's words! Alas!

Tidbits

— (Wu Xiongjian)

"One mouth, two pieces of skin, turning it over and over, it's always him!" This saying is really true. For example, if a poor person goes to a banquet and gorges himself, someone next to him will say, "He looks like he hasn't eaten in several lifetimes, just like he's grabbing medicine rice." If he is restrained and cautious, someone else will say, "This kind of person has never been to a decent gathering, just looking at him is enough to make me full!"

Records of Faint Fragrance of Imperial Incense

— Originally written by Princess Der Ling of Qing, translated by Qin Shouou

After that, we went back to a small informal hall in the center, and the Empress Dowager was ready to go back to her seat to rest: suddenly, she saw a very lively wooden horse standing alone in a not very bright corner. Its size and height were exactly the same as a real horse, and its four legs seemed to be deeply planted in the bricks and soil as if they were growing out of it. On its back, there was also a complete saddle, with countless shiny metal nail heads nailed to the saddle. | Perhaps they were originally nailed with jewels, but were later replaced. | At first, she seemed very surprised, then hurried over to examine it carefully, slowly nodding her head to show that she already understood: but we still couldn't figure out its purpose, and Guangxu remained lazy and paid no attention at all. So the Empress Dowager's chatterbox opened again.

"The most indispensable skills for a hunter are archery and horsemanship. We have already seen the learning of archery; now, this wooden horse is specially provided for practicing horsemanship! Because the most important and most difficult thing to learn in horsemanship is the speed and agility of mounting a horse. For example, if we encounter a wild animal and shoot it with one or two arrows, it has already fallen to the ground and seems to be dead. We have to ride over to take a look, but it is still lying motionless. So we always think that we can dismount to skin it or tie it up and take it away: unexpectedly, as soon as we dismount, it jumps up again. At this time, we must use the most skilled posture to jump onto the horse, otherwise, we will fall into its trick and lose our lives. Therefore, many of our past leaders often came here to use this wooden horse to practice the posture of mounting a horse: often they would practice continuously for several hours, sweating all over before they were willing to rest. (225)

Goods from Afar

— Zhang Huang

During the year of promoting national goods for women, the fashionable women in the cities invariably regarded high-heeled leather shoes made of goods from afar as the starting point of fashion. They are accustomed to it and do not find it strange, which is really strange! Take my cousin, who has long been recognized as the most knowledgeable among the female relatives, but she has not been able to escape this custom. A pair of high-heeled leather shoes is always on her feet. She said: "I am very willing to promote national goods, but the annoying thing is that the sound of these high-heeled leather shoes making a creaking sound when walking seems to be tempting, making me feel that without wearing them, I don't even have any energy. Even if I want to persuade others to use national goods, I can't speak up. I can only decide on my own that under the condition that I personally use all national goods, I will retain the matter of these high-heeled leather shoes."

One day, she invited me to accompany her to a leather shoe store opened by a Westerner to buy shoes, because she knew that one of her friends had recently bought satisfactory goods in this store. She thought that buying foreign goods would be cheaper. I thought that it would not be bad to accompany her to see the situation in a Western store. So four feet (I mean two people) walked into this shoe store full of exotic flavor.

There were five or six Westerners and one or two Chinese in the shoe store. I guessed that the Chinese would definitely be the ones to greet us when we Chinese came to patronize, | the so-called "birds of a feather flock together." Unexpectedly, a young Westerner rushed forward, and opened his mouth in English to say please sit down. Then, as if he had realized the inappropriateness of conversing with us in English while we hesitated to answer, he switched to a half-baked Chinese Mandarin to carry out his business procedures. He very quickly took out a pair of new-style leather shoes, and after looking at my cousin's foot size, he sat on a low stool to try them on for her, asking diligently if they were comfortable. According to her, they were really comfortable on her feet. When asked about the price, it was five dollars, which was indeed the lowest price. Such a pair of new-style leather shoes is on the market in Shanghai.

Of course, my cousin did not make any harsh objections to this price; but this unusually low price led her to suspect sloppiness in the workmanship, so she raised this question to this goods-from-afar clerk.

The goods-from-afar clerk's smiling and excited reply seemed to have anticipated this move. He said, "Please see, such sturdy and new-style workmanship is extremely trustworthy, because all the goods in our store are made by machines. One person manages the machine and produces hundreds of pairs a day, replacing the manual labor of several people, who can only produce a few pairs a day, so naturally the value is undoubtedly low."

A clear explanation immediately concluded the transaction. When we took the new shoes and went out, I saw a smug look of victory on the face of the goods-from-afar clerk, which seemed to be a source of pride for the industrial development of his country. But in my feelings, I only felt that this person who had traveled across the ocean to make a living had his livelihood taken away by huge machines and was still unaware of it, which was somewhat pitiful. Compared with the Chinese people's donation of money to increase the wealth and power of foreign countries, and their willingness to indulge in current vanity and enjoyment, it was only a matter of fifty steps compared to a hundred steps, wasn't it?

Recovery of Light

— Yue

Short story

Wrinkles on Yang Ershu's Forehead

— Die Yi

Uncle Yang Er, in the west street of Minghuang Town, could be considered the only well-to-do family. He had more than fifty acres of land, which was quite a lot in the countryside.

Every morning, Uncle Yang Er picked up his tile teapot and went to the teahouse in Zhongjie Street. After washing his face, he drank strong tea. The tea leaves were of the best Wuyi variety, which Uncle Yang Er provided himself. At the same time, he slowly cracked watermelon seeds. He was often the most eloquent person in the entire teahouse, and he was always so happy.

However, unfortunate luck gradually befell Uncle Yang Er! One year, he encountered troops passing through, and Uncle Yang Er was busy assigning everything he was responsible for supplying, which caused Uncle Yang Er to feel a heavy loss.

This year, the fields did have a good harvest, but unexpectedly the price of grain was very low, and the income was much worse than in previous years.

Following that, there were two years of flooding, and all the rice in the fields was drowned! The following year, there was a major drought, and the fields became cracked turtle shells, and there was no harvest at all.

Originally, relying on raising silkworms in the spring and summer seasons, he could earn dozens of dollars, but due to the depression of the silk industry, no silkworm cocoon shops were open, and there was no way to sell the cocoons, which was another major impact.

And more unfortunately, Yang Er's wife suffered from a very severe red-eye disease for more than three months. In addition to seeking medical treatment and taking medicine, she also sought secret prescriptions and made vows to Guanyin Temple, spending more than sixty dollars before ensuring that Yang Er's wife's eyes did not go blind and gradually regained their sight.

Under such repeated difficulties year after year, the money that Uncle Yang Er had accumulated through years of hard work was not only used up, but he also incurred a lot of debt.

As a result, in the teahouse on Zhongjie Street, it was rare to hear Uncle Yang Er's strong voice of conversation!

Soon, Uncle Yang Er's second son was about to marry a wife, and his second daughter was also about to get married. Although in such a famine year, everything could be simpler, the furniture in the son's new house and the daughter's dowry had to be prepared, which would cost a lot of money.

Uncle Yang Er thought about selling his water buffalo, but in such a year, everyone was planning the same thing as Uncle Yang Er, so who would buy his cow?

In the end, Uncle Yang Er had no choice but to sell a portion of his own land to others to solve the immediate difficulties.

In previous years, each acre of land could be worth at least two hundred dollars, but now no one wants it even for fifty dollars an acre. Uncle Yang Er finally entrusted someone and ran around himself several times, spending countless words, before he finally reached an agreement with Shao, the owner of the pharmacy in East Street. Six acres of land were valued at two hundred and fifty yuan. After signing the contract, Uncle Yang Er's six acres of land changed hands.

Out of the two hundred and fifty dollars, a portion was used to pay off debts that could no longer be delayed, and there was not much left. Uncle Yang Er worried every day about how to live in the days to come?

Originally, Uncle Yang Er had a very strong body and a radiant face, but now he often gets sick, and several deep wrinkles have appeared on his forehead!

Page 17

Free Talk

On Tea-Drinking Literature

— Zai Qing

Tea-drinking is an "elegant matter," but the privilege of this elegant matter belongs to "mountain men" and "famous scholars." Therefore, since ancient times, those who have discussed this matter most vigorously and reliably belong to this group. As for country bumpkins and peddlers, even if they are tired, they have to run into a small teahouse to drink some tea, which is just for rest and thirst quenching. There is no "tasting" or "elegance" involved. As for tea pickers, they basically have no good tea to drink. Being able to keep some "tea crumbs" and "tea stems" to enjoy with themselves and their neighbors is already something that ordinary people in the tea region do not have.

However, mountain men and famous scholars not only want to drink good tea, but also want to write poems about drinking tea and engrave exquisite collections of "tea-drinking literature." After Lu Yu's "The Classic of Tea," we have many books on drinking tea. I once saw a Ming Dynasty edition of "Tea Collection" which collected essays and poems about drinking tea since the Tang Dynasty. Before the book, there were also two pages of "Boiling Spring Picture" engraved by Tang Bohu, as well as inscriptions by many famous literary figures of the time. Drinking tea also requires good spring water, as can be imagined from the title of this "Boiling Spring Picture." Therefore, famous scholars who were particular about drinking tea at that time hired special ships to transport spring water from Huishan from afar, which is often seen in classics. Although Qiu Changru caused the "tea tasters" to be embarrassed once by mistaking river water for famous spring water and making a bit of a joke.

Zhong Bokjing wrote a "Collecting Rain Poem" with a short preface saying: "It has been raining continuously for days and nights, and there is no spring. Collecting it to brew the tea, the color and fragrance can rival Huiquan. The method is to use white cloth, five or six feet square, tie its four corners, and press it with a stone in the center to collect water from all directions, and place it in a jar in the courtyard to receive it. Those who avoid lightning dislike its impurity. All night long, I worry about the water not arriving, and then I no longer know the hardship of rain. Replacing annoyance with joy is also a way to change the environment with the mind." In helplessness, he actually came up with such a method to collect rain instead of famous spring water. For the sake of drinking tea, the painstaking effort can be generally seen; Zhang Zongzi sitting in Min Laozi's house, not leaving until he had drunk his famous tea, and only spending a day, what did that count for?

Also, the reason why Ran Dian loves to drink tea is good for comparison. The reason for loving tea is the same as "loving a beautiful woman." Enjoying oneself is also decorating oneself. I remember when Ximen Qing fell in love with Gui Jie, when he first invited guests to her house, Ying Bojue, seeing Ximen Qing's lust, once teased him with a "tea poem" in the tune of "Chao Tianzi" when serving tea. The poem said, "The tender buds of this fine tea grow in the spring breeze. If you don't pick or pluck them, the leaves will be residue. But boiling them gives them a great color. The exquisite quality is hard to describe or paint. I sip it often in the daytime, thinking of it when I'm drunk, and loving it when I wake up. Originally, a basket of it is worth a thousand gold." Comparing tea to a beautiful woman illustrates their consistent understanding of the two, although there are considerable differences between them.

However, drinking tea ultimately has prerequisite conditions, which is a stable life. Zhang Dafu was one of the best at drinking tea. In his "Complete Works" and "Pen Talks," if the articles on drinking tea were separated, they could also be printed into a book. Perhaps no one has researched drinking tea more deeply than him. However, while he was studying drinking tea, his wife actually came to bother him, saying that there was no rice in the kitchen, forcing him to put down the important matter of drinking tea and go to find money to buy rice and cook, and to express a sigh.

I bought a Japanese remnant book "Recent Words" from a cold stall at the City God Temple, which was written even more interestingly. It said: "A mountain monk loved tea, and a woodcutter passed by every day, and the monk always served him tea. The woodcutter said: "What virtue does tea have that the master loves it so much?" The monk said: "Drinking tea has three benefits, one is to aid digestion, two is to dispel sleep, and three is to reduce desires." The woodcutter said: "What the master calls the three benefits are all not for the benefit of the little man. The little man cuts firewood to provide food, and eats bean porridge and coarse food. If he loves digestive things, he is bound to be hungry. I move when it is light, and rest when it is dark, and sleep soundly, not waking until dawn, and the pleasure of a king facing south cannot surpass it. If he loves things that dispel sleep, he is bound to be hard-working. The little man has a wife who can share poverty with the little man, for the pleasure of sleeping together. If he loves things that reduce desires, he will make his wife unable to endure poverty. Therefore, all three are not for the benefit of the little man, and I dare to refuse." It can be seen that drinking tea is not a "pure blessing" that everyone can enjoy, except for those high-ranking officials and nobles, and mountain men and famous scholars.

Among the new literati, there is no shortage of people who talk about drinking tea and write tea-drinking literature. First, there was the poet Xu Zhimo, who died in "the wind does not know which way to blow," and later there was Sun Fuxi, who did the tea-drinking literature movement and ran a tea-drinking magazine. However, Xu the poet's "On Drinking Tea" has become a lost manuscript in his complete works, and Sun the painter's magazine also seems to have not continued for a long time. The best group left is probably only Zhou Zuoren, the master of the bitter tea hermitage, who says "let's go to my humble house to drink bitter tea." Zhou Zuoren started "drinking tea" from the "Rainy Day Book" era (1925) to the publication of "Watching Clouds Collection" (1933), and he was still "drinking tea," but when he was "fifty years old" (1934), he designated people to "drink bitter tea." Drinking tea to the point of drinking bitter tea, the high degree of his tea drinking is knowable, and the inevitability of his drinking tea is also knowable. However, we cannot but admire that the continuous domestic and foreign artillery fire has not smashed Zhou Zuoren's tea hermitage, teapot, and teacup. The life of a special class is so stable.

Eight or nine years ago, Ryunosuke Akutagawa visited Shanghai, and he satirized the "tea drinkers" on the Nine-Bend Bridge; During the Li Hongzhang era, foreigners also had the prediction that "seeing the Chinese people's 'drinking tea,' one can see that this country is hopeless." However, now, even in terms of the intellectual class, there are not only those who "entrust their grief to bitter tea," but also those who are tired of Chinese tea and advocate drinking foreign tea. This truly cannot but make people have a Kang Youwei-style sigh: "Alas"! I want to say nothing!

The Sound of Selling Cakes

— Ma Xingye

What makes people feel the saddest at night, in the past few months, was the weak sound of the passing geese. In winter, the sound of geese is no longer heard much. Every night, when you are not asleep or not sleeping deeply, you will always hear the sound of selling cakes in the alley. The neighbors often play cards, sometimes until dawn, so the cake seller knows that there are good customers here, and at three or four o'clock in the middle of the night, he still sings weakly about selling cakes, and the sound is full of sad emotions.

Recently, I have spent more time in the library, and my brain is tired, so my sleep has become abnormal. My school doctor once told me that if you run a mile or two desperately before going to bed, you will fall asleep and not know the dawn. I have tried it in the past, and it has worked, but after arriving in Nanjing, where can you run like a madman? The roads are full of mud, the alleys are full of coal gas, and walking around in the house interferes with the sleep of the friends downstairs.

I am afraid to hear and love to hear the sound of the cake seller, because the sound of the cake seller indicates that the night is very deep, and while many humans are already enjoying their God-given right to sleep, I am unfortunately abandoned. I do not resent it, because he is singing weakly, he is being oppressed by life, and in the cold wind and dew, he is watching the opportunity to sleep pass by. In his opinion, I am considered a relatively happy person. I unconsciously have a nameless feeling of friendship for the cake seller. I often wait with my eyes open for the arrival of this sound. Often I wait for a long time and the sound has not yet penetrated into the alley, and I worry: perhaps he is sick today, or there is a night show, and something dangerous has happened.

Recently, the house has been cleaned very cleanly, my heart is not disturbed, and my brain is not reminiscing, and I am staring alone with my slightly dry eyes, aimlessly looking at the four walls. If the night is not too dark, I can also see many maps on the wall, seriously scowling at me. The fire in the stove is out, and a line of cold wind is drilling into the small holes of the wire window. At this time, there is only one me in the world. I weakly put my body on the bed, and let the bed steadily support my entire weight and the weight of my emptiness. My heart is like still water, like a deep abyss, and the slow and sad sound of selling cakes is like cold wine pouring into fresh water, slowly penetrating in and sinking down.

I often hear the sound of horns in the middle of the night, and I have also heard the sound of ancient temple bells in a state of semi-sleep, but neither is as unforgettable as the sound of the cake seller. A certain Japanese person once wrote an article about the trumpet at night, and recalled many terrors of war from the sound of the trumpet. When I was in middle school, I was very moved when I read that novel, but at that time, I had no experience of insomnia, so I could not appreciate all its wonderfulness. Four or five years ago in Nanjing, I gradually began to understand the meaning of this text. Wen Zhengming of the Ming Dynasty has an essay "Record of the Drum Sound of the Offering Tower," from which he realized the feelings of many unfortunate people in the world. When I went home last summer and stayed quietly for more than twenty days, the Xiantan Temple in the east of the city often rang bells and drums in the middle of the night, so I knew Wen Zhengming's state of mind in those years. Time is gradually sending me, and my ability to understand the state of mind of others is gradually improving. Life is a plum branch, and the branch is full of many joys and sorrows, and these bell sounds, trumpet sounds, and cake-selling sounds can also be regarded as a few small buds on this plum branch.

Huang Zhongze was a talented poet, and his decadence is what I think is most unacceptable, although it is very sympathetic. Among his many clear and beautiful little poems like the cry of a crane on a clear night, I like to read this one: "In the morning, light rain makes it difficult to form a dream, everywhere I hear the selling of maltose by the stream. No wonder the peach blossoms are half fallen, tomorrow will be Qingming in the riverside village." After all, what kind of sound is "maltose flute"; I still don't know, but I can very well understand his state of mind of not being able to sleep on a rainy night, and being surprised that Qingming is coming again. This kind of artistic conception is completely different from that of "listening to the spring rain in a small building all night, selling apricot blossoms in a deep alley tomorrow morning." One is unwilling to see the arrival of Qingming, and the other is very interested in selling apricot blossoms tomorrow, and has warm pleasure.

I don't know if the cake seller will be an old man or a young man. If he is a young man, his voice will at least carry the sorrow of an adult. I don't know when he can go to sleep. I myself will always fall asleep groggily at five or four o'clock. During the day, when I am already sitting in the library, or leaning against the fire by the stove, I don't know where the cake seller is. I hope he can get a sweet sleep.

Random Notes from Guizhou (Part 2)

— Especially

Passing Lou Mountain Pass

In a small, damp house, five or six lamps could be lit, filling the air with swirling smoke:

"One basin isn't enough today. We'll have to sell our strength later!"

"Let's split another basin, huh? Crossing Lou Mountain Pass, three ups and three downs, is tough enough."

This small house doesn't need any "Do Not Discuss State Affairs" notices. Although their words are all disordered, even facts from the past decade and fantasies about the next few years flow casually from their mouths, "state affairs" are irrelevant to them. They don't care who is feuding with whom, or who is celebrating with whom. These things are like external matters that have nothing to do with them.

"Not hurrying yet? The sun's halfway up the sky! This bunch of turtles!" The foreman searched anxiously along the long street of the village, from east to west.

Like a whirlpool of rushing water, people rushed towards the center from different openings.

"Put in some extra effort to get through the pass today, and we'll have a good meal at the inn tonight. (Note)" The foreman smiled, offering them some encouraging comfort.

We set off, a mighty group, advancing along this long mountain road.

On the road, you could also see passing travelers. At least, you could see many donkeys carrying goods. Without access to foreign ships or trains, everything needed to rely on their physical strength to transport daily necessities.

Besides lodging and having a quick meal, stopping along the mountain road was also important. Large stations were ten to fifteen li apart, and small stations were three to five li apart. The distances weren't very accurate, but those who traveled the route frequently could estimate where to eat and where to rest. Once these places were decided, there were very few stops at other stations.

The natural scenery in the mountain hollows was quite lovely: dense trees, beautiful green mountains, clear streams, terraced fields, and the endless, bumpy roads all slipped away beneath our feet, slipped away. However, "mountains seem to run away as you approach." Lou Mountain Pass, which didn't seem far away, actually took more than three hours to reach.

We had another quick meal and ate a little more food. Then, we started to climb the mountain pass. Lou Mountain wasn't that high, but the stone steps were quite steep, causing the travelers' legs to ache and their strength to weaken.

The second peak was higher, and the last one was the highest. Usually, there are some flat stretches between two mountains, but Lou Mountain Pass had continuous ups and downs, leaving the weary body no chance to recover. Perhaps this was why it was considered so difficult?

With great difficulty, we climbed to the final summit. Involuntarily, we all took a deep breath and sat down. The sun was already setting.

The foreman's face was smiling, and he was humming:

Lou Mountain is high and deep,

Shoulders carry heavy loads, so heavy,

Three ups and three downs, eighteen li,

Clothes soaked with sweat, exhausting.

Note: Sedan chair, a mode of transportation in Guizhou. Tarpaulin, a waterproof cloth that must be placed on top of the sedan chair to prevent rain. A good meal, meaning a treat.

Abandoned Woman

— Written by 丨丨Maud Jousey Fangel

The Human World (3)

— Li Huiying

This time, without my friend answering me, I knew where we were because as soon as I entered the room, I smelled a strong odor of opium. What else could this be but an opium den? But opium dens should be located on busy streets to attract customers. How could they have business hidden in a dark alley? The few opium dens I saw on Zhengyang Street were not only brightly decorated with brilliant lights, but they also had people standing at the door soliciting business. As you passed by, they would say to you:

"Original raw opium, original product; take a puff, it's really better."

Or:

"The opium tastes good, no other place can compare; the bubbles are big, smoking costs half the price."

Since this place was an opium den, why didn't my friend say so? Could there be some unspeakable secret hidden in this?

We first walked into a dark hall, and then into a small room to the right of the hall. My friend walked through the dark room as if he knew it better than the dark roads in the alleys, as if it were his own home. In the darkness, I saw a kang (brick bed) by the window. My guide grabbed something on the kang in the darkness, and immediately a shrill female cry came out. Only then did I realize that there was a woman lying on the kang. The woman then spoke:

"Is it Cao, Master? What, did your wife at home let you off the leash?"

This sentence contained a strong hint of sarcasm, but it was said so bluntly that anyone could guess the woman's identity.

A small kerosene lamp, about the size of a bean, was lit by the young girl who had followed us into the room. I carefully looked around the room: it was an opium den, no doubt about it – the five or six opium trays placed on the kang were the most powerful evidence. This woman, about twenty-four or twenty-five years old, looked unkempt and feisty, clearly a female rogue, and an opium addict. In short, she was someone who mattered.

My friend spoke:

"What's the point of saying that? What do you mean, 'let me off the leash'? If you didn't want me to stay every day, you wouldn't have kept me."

Saying such words was indeed a bit harsh, but saying them to a woman of her status could not be considered an insult. On the contrary, she wanted you to say some similar things to her so that she could be happy. As expected, after hearing my friend's words, she cried even more and said:

"As long as you have dollars, you can stay for ten or fifteen days at your leisure."

This place is an opium den, a private opium den, and at the same time it is also a private brothel.

I completely understood this place.

"Okay, talking idle talk is useless. I'll introduce you to a customer," my friend pinched her face and said. "This is my friend Li Weixing, director of a certain section of the police department; this is," he pointed to her with a smile, "this is my lover, my lover Hao Xiaolan."

Correction: In the article "The Anti-Mountain Humanistic Literature of the Late Ming Dynasty" published the other day, Xue Gang hated Shanren (mountain man) so much that he changed "Shanren" to "Shanjī" (mountain chicken), which was mistakenly printed as "Shanzá" (mountain mongrel). We hereby correct this error.

Commercial News

Financial and Gold Markets Remain Unstable

Rebound After a Fall, Recovering 3.7 Yuan

Yesterday, the gold market was filled with uncertainty and hesitation. Initially, it fell due to the strengthening of the foreign exchange market. However, positive news and intervention from the central bank stimulated buying, eventually pushing the price above 70 yuan. The buying frenzy was intense. In the morning, the overseas silver market was stable in both the UK and the US, but brokers predicted that the US would rise after the market closed, and the forward silver price in Montréal actually fell. Foreign exchange rates generally rebounded. London spot gold fell 10 pence. Premarket trading opened and quickly dropped to 67.8 yuan, then rose to 68.9 yuan. The central bank's official exchange rates were announced, with the British rate unchanged and the US rate up 0.0625. The customs gold unit fell 0.012. The standard gold price retreated to 988.7 yuan, then weakened slightly after that. The supply of gold continued to surge after the opening, causing the price to continue to fall, but there was strong support to maintain the price at the lower level. The market was generally stable, allowing for some upward movement. However, major players continued to sell aggressively. The central bank supplied spot silver, and Sassoon sold forward silver, which kept downward pressure on the market. Banks seized the opportunity to buy at cheap prices, and the foreign exchange market potentially tightened. Buyers became active in the market, gradually pushing the price back up. The silver balance tax was announced, but there were no changes. At this time, the HSBC bought forward silver, tightening the foreign exchange market, and the price rose above 9 yuan. After the high, suppliers tried to balance the market, struggling slightly. However, major players sold off in droves, making it difficult to avoid a decline. However, the overall trend was stable, and there was strong support to maintain the price at the lower level. Major players also bought after selling. Although there were some rebounds, trading in the market was sluggish, and the trend remained mediocre, hovering around 8 yuan. The market became more stable at noon. In the afternoon, the foreign exchange market continued to strengthen, and sellers continued to surge and fall. However, due to the slight reduction in the printing of silver, there were many buying orders after the low. When the central bank intervened with spot gold, and the Associated Press in Nanjing reported positive news for the buying side, the price rebounded. However, it continued to fluctuate. Later, as market sentiment turned positive, the foreign exchange market tightened, and the central bank continued to intervene with spot silver, pushing the price above 70 yuan. Although there were some setbacks due to major players taking profits, eager buying and rumors favorable to the buying side fueled the market. The closing price was very strong. The overall trend for the day was uncertain, and the market was jittery. Overnight interbank lending rates fell to 0.15 yuan. Swap premiums also fell to around 7 yuan. The day's market conditions are recorded below.

The market opened in the morning at 967.98 yuan, 1.3 yuan lower than the previous close. Fuxing, Yongchang, Dayuan, Maoyong, Dafayong, Hengchangyong, and others sold bars, retreating to 6.4 yuan. Hengyu, Yongli, Jinlong, Fuyu, Fusheng, Hengxing, and others bought at the lower price. McCallum bought US dollars for March at 1.875, rising to 8.5 yuan. It was rumored that the central bank sold spot silver at 1.875 to Wah Bi. Fuxing, Yongda, Decheng, Hengyu, Dafayong, Yuanyong, Maoyong, Yongfeng, Zhaofengchang, and others sold, gradually moving downward. Sassoon sold June silver at 6.875, retreating to 5.7 yuan. Yesterday's soybean market situation, bearing the previous day's rising wind, prices continued to rise, the factory sold a large batch of cakes the previous day, its soybean stomach is still not stagnant, counting the purchase of Dalian Siping Street soybeans ten cars, the price of four yuan zero one cent, and Bengbu soybeans one car, this street and the inland, etc. taken Hankou Zha soybeans more than two thousand bags, Dalian Fan Yutun soybeans two hundred bags, Shashi soybeans more than two hundred bags, Han Chi soybeans two hundred and fifty bags, Tongzhou to do Yingzhou soybeans one car, now the general situation due to the arrival of the two thin, the market is stable, sesame foreign goods continued to open five hundred tons, by Sassoon to do, the price opened nine yuan nine jiao half, Zhenjiang to take one hundred tons, the price of nine yuan nine jiao, the current goods East Ocean to do and to do net goods of the stomach is still connected, so the market is stable.

Bran Guest Firms Also Lack of Procurement

Bran market, because foreign wheat does not move, inland help is to account for the near day, unless there is an urgent need, are less interested, so the turnover of goods market is weak, quite a trend of weakness, yesterday opened Fufeng bran two yuan six jiao half, Fuxin bran two yuan six jiao two points.

North and South Goods Raw Peanuts Rebounded

Raw peanuts Qingdao news rebounded, Shen city followed the tight, and Guangdong sales also see active, yesterday a total of one hundred and ten tons, such as Kaifeng Ren Zhou two opened seven yuan two angles, yesterday opened seven yuan four corners, a good start two jiao, Guide Ren six yuan six corners, Xuzhou Ren called to rise two or three jiao, not completed, the market felt quite firm.

Xiamen Dried Meat Rose Five or Six Jiao

Xiamen dried round meat, recent rounds of no arrival, check the market is rare, the number of goods is even more scarce, so the trend is turning tight, coupled with the current higher goods, this street is quite a need, so the opening price is good to start five or six angles, are the line to do, the number of goods has been sold, the next batch to be, if the identity is dry, the color is bright red, and no black pieces, the future is still to prevent the continued tight.

Yesterday's sugar market, coarse sand white because the customs gold saw a drop, and the existing goods increased and the purchase decreased, the price is back down, domestic Chaoqing also has a slight loose, the Association of Hua Pan, twenty-four coarse sand white spot ordinary eighteen yuan seven jiao, compared with the previous day fell angle half, transfer of goods five yuan four corners half, unchanged, eight nine red load thirteen yuan nine jiao, no transaction, Taikoo sugar B Mark nineteen yuan two corners, compared with the previous day and a small five points, this factory cotton white unchanged, one number is still eighteen yuan three jiao, number plate has Chao help to open Chaoqing more than two thousand bags, the price of twelve yuan eight jiao to ten yuan two jiao, Guangbang opened Zhu Qing one hundred bags, the price of ten yuan two jiao, yesterday Guangdong round by Shantou entry, there are Chaoqing and Zhiyang Zhichi sugar two thousand nine hundred and thirty-two bags.

Textiles Cold Weather Overcoat Business Soared

Recently the weather suddenly turned cold, woolen overcoat business thus soared, Da Xin Street area now buy men and women overcoats, are very prosperous, however, for the feed side, is still very little, cover is too late, most are planning to end, so in addition to selling their own inventory, there is no more added, resulting in the main road woolen market, there is still no better image.

Oil Market Foreign White Tung Oil Shanghai and Wuhan Are Both Moving

Since the white tung oil market turned tight in Wuhan, the Wuhan banks have raised the price of guest goods to more than 26 yuan per dan for Xiangtong, and foreign merchants want to raise it to 32 yuan for foreign rules. Although the foreign banks are unwilling, due to the lack of sources and the demand exceeding supply, the buyers cannot hold on for long. There are also a lot of goods sold by foreign banks in this port. According to the past two days, a total of 300 tons were exported, which were sold before. In recent days, there have also been dozens and hundreds of tons of transactions, and the price is 32 yuan and four jiao per dan, including iron barrels and customs duties, which will probably be delivered next month. However, what the foreign banks in this port have imported is Zhejiang tung. Since the new goods were produced, there have been more than a thousand tons of transactions, and there are still many that have not been delivered. Although the production of Zhejiang tung has increased year by year, if the demand from foreign merchants is so high, it is still not enough to meet the demand. Therefore, the market in Hangzhou has raised the price of full-weight goods to 27 yuan and two jiao per zhui delivered to Shanghai, which has increased by more than one yuan in two or three days, always affected by the Shanghai foreign exchange.

Hardware Black Sheet Iron Almost a Discontinued Item

After the black sheet iron arrived in large quantities, the market was flooded with inventory. The outlet is due to Tianjin's entry, and the Yantai, Qingdao, and Weihaiwei areas have also reduced their embellishment. The market is extremely cold. The porcelain enamel factory in this street has also stopped buying because American Yellow Eagle brand goods have arrived in large quantities. It is almost a discontinued item among hardware products. It is reported that there were only thirty or forty bundles of transactions in the market yesterday. The price of three-foot six-foot is estimated at 9 yuan two or three jiao per dan, and two-foot six-foot is sold at 9 yuan one or two jiao per bundle.

Shen Bao Local Supplement

Talks

The Price of Sacrifice

—Bored

Our country's ancient philosophy of life has many clear teachings and creeds, such as "A wise man protects himself," "A man who knows fate does not stand under a crumbling wall," "A son of a thousand gold should not sit under a drooping eave," etc., all of which are appropriate ways to assess the situation and protect one's life. A more meaningful and superhuman philosophy is expressed by Mencius: "Life is what I desire, and righteousness is also what I desire. If I cannot have both, I will give up life for righteousness." Later, Song Confucian scholars elaborated on this meaning, saying that "Losing integrity is a major matter, while starvation is a minor matter." They saw integrity and righteousness as more important than life. Apart from that, there is nothing more important than life itself. This is why the land of Eastern culture has stood alone for thousands of years.

Foreigners are, after all, barbarians. They do not view life as so important. As long as they succeed in their careers, they can disregard their lives. They have a spirit of adventure, great ambition, and are not afraid of thousands of difficulties. They are determined to do whatever it takes. Just like exploring the temperate zone, the North and South Poles, crossing the Atlantic by plane, and flying around the world in a week, they do not understand the danger of life, they only know that the goal can be achieved. Young people in our country have recently understood some of the philosophy of life. Therefore, they do not value their own lives very much. Therefore, cases of suicide have emerged one after another, countless. But upon investigating the reasons for suicide, there are only two: (1) economic oppression, and (2) heartbreak, or being unable to achieve the goal of love due to economic oppression. Besides this, I have not heard of any particularly valuable sacrifices. I ask, what value exists in such sacrifices?

But recently there has been genuine progress. Just turn to the recent newspapers. Haven't you seen that pedestrian Pan Deming is about to return home? Haven't you seen the heroic feat of elementary school students traveling around the country? Haven't you seen a Chinese female aviator flying from Kuala Lumpur to Singapore? Indeed, these individuals all have a spirit of adventure, and it cannot be said that they have absolutely no meaning. This is something I deeply admire. But now is the world of flying, not the world of walking. Such a round-the-world walking endeavor only increases personal experience and knowledge, and does not make a great contribution to society and the country. As for the female aviator's flight, the flight from Kuala Lumpur to Singapore is only a little over two hundred miles. In the eyes of us Chinese, it is already a remarkable thing, but in the eyes of foreigners, it is still insignificant.

But this kind of thing is indeed considered a rare heroic feat in our country. The nature of our Chinese people is often to take a derisive attitude. When they succeed in their careers, they only feel jealous and suspicious. If they fail, they will ridicule in every way. Therefore, if someone wants to do something, they must first consider whether they can succeed. Success is good, but if it fails, they will be ridiculed by others. In this way, the courage to do this will disappear without a trace. Therefore, to do something, one does not have to ask whether it will succeed or fail, but only ask whether it should be done or not. If I think it is something that should be done, I will boldly do it. Success or failure is certainly not a concern, and let them laugh and scold! Only then can

My First Acquaintance with Winter

— Shi Jingbo

My grandfather was a very amiable old man, tall and large in stature, a most typical northerner, with a long beard, a few strands of which were golden and gleaming, the rest pale and fluffy, adorning his kind and approachable face, making him especially respectable.

He managed his extremely complex family affairs with great diligence and remarkable patience. Within that huge and complicated household, he indeed succeeded, being a model of perseverance. Later, he used this strength to create his own family business, character, and historically significant achievements, struggling up from a declining merchant family, striving to study, and teaching my eldest uncle and my father to read as well. My second and third uncles farmed, their own land not being enough, so they rented land from others. Although his family business did not fulfill his perfect hopes, on the basis of the significance of striving in life, he gained the respect and faith of the entire society.

He passed away from incurable cerebral hemorrhage at the age of sixty-one. I was only five years old at that time, and it was then that I first came to know the face of winter.

On the night of the seventh day of the twelfth month, he, my eldest uncle, and my father returned from somewhere. I remember it was a very cold night. My grandmother took me to the center of the courtyard to look towards the stone path opposite, finally seeing them return. I was the first to see a faintly shining light appear at the end of the stone path. My grandmother immediately determined it was my grandfather and the others returning. Sure enough, we opened the gate, and it really was my grandfather and the others returning. The shining light turned out to be their paper lanterns.

I don't remember what happened later. Vaguely, it seems my grandfather carried me to my mother's room to sleep, but I knew nothing.

I don't know who carried me to another room, and I woke up. I immediately felt that a tremendous event had erupted in my sleep. A miserable, painful, and despairing atmosphere immediately seized me, refusing to let go. I contracted a very severe case of typhoid fever.

Page 20

The disease immediately spread to my eldest brother.

I was staying in my mother's birthing room. On one heated brick bed (炕), slept my mother, my newborn younger sister, my two eldest brothers and I, all suffering from severe typhoid fever, and my maternal grandmother, who was sixty or seventy years old. Sometimes, my grandmother and eldest aunt also slept there. Strangely, in such a dirty and foul-smelling world, our typhoid fever did not spread to a third person.

By the time I regained consciousness, my grandfather had already been buried. I saw my mother sitting on the edge of the heated brick bed, covered in a quilt, and heard the baby crying. Beside me, my eldest brother lay unconscious. The windows were covered with something, making it difficult to see the light outside, which was very stifling; but I couldn't move at all, not even having the strength to turn over.

I remember that winter passed like this. This was my first acquaintance with winter, and the first time since I had life that I knew there was a severe winter. In human society, I first vaguely developed a conscious relationship with nature, which was when I began to understand the seasonality of social life.

Winter in this seasonality is almost a huge threat and ravagement for the working people.

A Story of Life

— Hu Weixiong

He added a lump of coal to the fireplace for the third time, a move that elicited laughter from the other person.

The fireplace was originally blazing with flames, but he extinguished them by shoveling in lumps of coal one after another, instead raising a pungent coal smoke.

Would you say he lacked experience with fireplaces? That's far from the truth. He could make delicious dishes on a gas stove, and could immediately fix a fuse after the electric lights went out, mend socks and sew clothes. When necessary, he could even do a thing or two... His various experiences could be compiled into a profitable encyclopedia. What he lacked was the knack for dealing with women, and this woman had knocked on his bedroom door five minutes ago.

"It's too cold to go outside for a walk, but you haven't learned the skill of lighting a fireplace!" The woman's affected voice burst into laughter.

This sentence was not without reason: he often escaped from his apartment because of her disturbances, wandering aimlessly until he could no longer support his tired body and returned home. Using such a clumsy method to escape a woman he didn't like only further stimulated her unspeakable feelings, causing her to entangle herself in his apartment day and night.

Tonight, the wind exposed the true face of winter, naturally unsuitable for a stroll leaning on a cane. He had knocked on the doors of several friends, but these urbanites had all gone to the frenzied dance halls. So, he thought of catching the 9:15 movie, but returning to the apartment after it ended would still be too early, so he went home with the thought that tonight might be an exception, planning to brew tea and read. As he was facing the fireplace, lying in a rocking chair and swinging his legs, footsteps sounded in the hallway.

His bedroom was the last one in the apartment. Without a doubt, the footsteps had reached the door by the time people inside could hear them clearly. Sure enough, there was a gentle knock on the door, but the visitor had already anticipated there would be no answer, barging in like a Chinese manager entering a compradore's office, taking off her coat, hanging it behind the door, and dragging another rocking chair to sit next to him to warm herself by the fireplace.

The host's attitude of ignoring her was an old trick. While reading the newspaper, he folded it haphazardly, and when facing the fireplace, of course, he worked hard at adding coal.

He heard her sarcastic remarks and finally raised his head, spitting out words that seemed to have been prepared:

"Aren't you afraid of the cold? Coming such a long way!"

"Isn't there a fireplace here!"

The host couldn't answer with a second sentence. Flames bursting from the coal licked at two crimson faces like serpent tongues, a deadly silence except for their breaths.

In these few minutes, let me introduce the female guest's outline!

She was known as some kind of social butterfly, and the men hanging on her arm were as changeable as her clothes. She was immersed in a decadent lifestyle, so she sought stimulation. Naturally, wouldn't men be the best targets? However, since she discovered this man who was inept with women, she seemed to have discovered the most powerful stimulant in the world. Thus, this corner of the apartment was staging this farcical tragedy.

Of course, we cannot predict the outcome before the curtain falls.

But humans are the soul of all things. This kind of trick is being acted out everywhere just right; big fights, small quarrels, this story can be created at will, seeing the opportunity and acting. Life is like a stage, can you not believe this saying?

Mr. Wen Kegang's Calligraphy

Recent Works by Mr. Wu Gonghu

Hesitation at Dusk

— A Chun

Girls are afraid of autumn, but I am most afraid of that gloomy dusk!

It is a distorted winter. The drizzle is continuous, without any wind at all. In the quietness, there is only the rhythm of the clock. Every corner of the room is filled with an elusive emptiness. Sitting alone, letting my long dress drag on the ground, letting my soul be free, letting my thoughts be liberated, giving myself an honest dissection of everything I have stored, in this gloom of dusk, internal contradictions surge!

Surrounded by a rosy circle, a child who doesn't understand anything strangely obtains inexplicable joy like a free little bird. When the roses of May unfold, a beautiful spring story has already begun!

It was an early summer evening. Darkness had filled the earth. The evening breeze brought sparse raindrops. The distant shimmering lights and the hustle and bustle on the Waibaidu Bridge were truly the beginning of a night metropolis. The two of us were on the grass under the trees, watching our slanting shadows disappear, all the way to hearing the waves of the river, seeing off the leisurely chats of the wandering immortals, still hesitating in our lingering. At that time, the moon girl had some light, and the waves surged even more eagerly forward. Besides the distant commotion coming from the night metropolis, there was also that foolish man who mourned the fallen nation nearby! Gradually, a blur had enveloped the surroundings, and everything disappeared with it, as if only our two ardent hearts remained in this large world! Without the hypocrisy of morality, without the cruel iron armor, shedding the shackles of unfreedom, we showed the naked sparks of spring. He gripped my hand tightly:

"I won't leave you, Chun! I will never leave you!"

"... Martyrdom." Smiling, I lowered my head.

"What method is there to never leave you, Chun!"

"What method do you say there is?"

"Let's 'that'!"

When I understood his intentions, it was as if I had received an unexpected thunderbolt. Truly, I hadn't expected him to mention this issue so quickly. Silently, I said nothing, waiting until he let go of my hand and gave me a final kiss, I still silently lowered my head and left him.

At night, I hurriedly burrowed into bed, covering my head with the quilt. The entire night, I couldn't find a sleep demon. Truly, I was immersed in the pain of contradiction again!

Without being deceived by the "sacred," and without thinking about the coming of any grave, only the terrible life of a mother began in my imagination! Ah! I will not be a child! I will lose my freedom, I will pass away in the obligatory life of a family, and I will climb to another stage!

"No, I will never agree, I must prolong my golden age!"

"No, I will never agree, I must not quickly end my free life!"

In my heart, I made such a definite resolution.

The next day, I rushed to his place and expressed some childish thoughts, saying that we should postpone it for another year or two, right?

I thought it should be a cold reply. When I also thought, in the same way, of "not being able to live without him," I regretted my words again!

Now, in this dusk, given the prolonged contemplation, given the past remains, given his burly, lovely shadow, I am immersed in hesitation again!

Between people, some similar things are unavoidable. A woman can never escape those inevitable stages. Why should I deliberately make myself suffer?

Giving way to this conclusion, I hurried away from the hesitation of dusk!

Evening Voyage

— Ding Weinan

This is an autumn.

The dried-up river water shows the leanness of the riverbed. The gray-black small reefs reveal their desolate aura, bringing the sparse barking of dogs. This is the slight ripple rippling in the gentle breeze. The boatmen row what poets call a small leaf boat, floating on this babbling river and going up to the ancient castle. The so-called one-leaf boat, when rowed by these boatmen, is truly more difficult than going up the Shu Road. The people pulling the towline on the shore have their waists aching. The person at the helm is very strong, but the slowness of the voyage is still struggling in this river bay for a day.

From the faint light of dawn, one can see the Longtan Pagoda emerging from the horizon. In the light of the sunrise, bathing in its mixture of mountains and clouds, it stands majestic and clear on that protruding hill, like a proud bamboo shoot, also like a straight pen. Next to it is a temple surrounded by it. It stands proudly in the center of this temple, towering. The white surrounding wall of the temple is so small and squatting at its feet, like a white collar on the neck of a Westerner. In people's sight, this pagoda releases immense dignity. The copper gourd on top of the pagoda reflects golden light under the oblique rays of the setting sun, dazzling people's eyes, like a seashell on the beach, shimmering and trembling with the pulse of nature in this evening on that distant horizon, nurturing the embryo of the night!

The struggling people finally dragged the bottom of the boat forward, although the river water was dry and the bones were exposed. Gradually, they were sailing near Longtan under the pagoda. The river water was gradually getting deeper. The pagoda was slowly rising towards us, its outline even clearer. The river water was deep and green. The matter of pulling the towline still could not reduce the boatmen's

Page 21

work. The wind was light, almost unable to stir up the slight ripples of the river water, but it stirred up the people's bodies, and there was almost a lot of coolness. Although the reeds over there were a little swaying, a little floating, the shadows falling in the water, given the wave marks on the bottom of the boat going upstream, shattered her tenderness in that water. Those slender shadows seem to be whispering! Geese sometimes raise their flight from their clusters, which will startle their fragile souls, but on their bodies is crystallized the deep news of autumn, and the quiet moan in the brewing of this night!

Gradually, it became blurred. The majestic shadow of the pagoda fell in the pool. There are many ships sailing to and from here, raising white sails, destroying the shadow of the pagoda bathing in the pool in this vast twilight. Shaking, trembling sky! In the cabin of the ship, the lights were lit, and cooking was beginning. Looking down at the bottom of the water, one can only see the white sky, and the drifting idle clouds, but if you look carefully underneath, it is dark and a little frightening, like things from mythology, appearing before your eyes. If the white sky and the drifting idle clouds all disappear, the changing components will not be destroyed.

That ancient castle is also appearing vaguely. The moon is rising, hanging in the eastern sky. I don't know where the sound of the bell is, deeply knocking on the heart of the traveler who is embarking on the journey. If it is said that this will not bring good news to the traveler, it must be a deeply painful departure!

The voyagers are all holding frightened hearts. The turbulent era has brought unrest in the countryside. The ancient castle over there in the vastness is a symbol of comfort for people, especially at this moment. The vast night, with the sound of the water of the boat moving forward, rocking the shadow of the moon, breaking the stars, carrying the heart of a traveler, floats on this vast journey!

Temptation

— Luo Shan

(Your sons are living off their mother's tears, do you really want to go back or not?)

It was a bitterly cold winter dusk. I was shrinking and sitting by the stove, warming myself and leisurely reading Browning's lyric poetry, poetry, to express to my passionately loved woman. I remember I made a face and called him my friend, stopping mid-sentence for fear of causing some kind of misunderstanding between us. I merely answered with a bitter smile!

(Life's process is in this way, you understand my life philosophy, don't you? This is the powerful proof of my life philosophy!)

Indeed, that friend's words did not stimulate even a single fiber in me, and I was very surprised. I understood very well the desert sands and hurricanes of northern Mongolia in winter, the construction and incomplete equipment of the house, the situation, the pity of the wife suffering from insomnia and neurasthenia. However, I did not feel a single bit of compassion for that pity. As for children, I, in my hedonism, thought it was a burden, a meaningless thing. However, on the third night after that friend left, under the bright electric lights, my lover and I were each looking at books with our heads lowered in a comfortable sofa, I discovered a piece of work that resembled a true depiction of my life. My heart trembled slightly, and then an uneasy life began, and I almost regarded the woman sitting next to me as an incarnation of the devil, and began to curse the blindness of life, the error of the starting point of complete individualism.

("Isn't the greatest mission of 'man' living in the world to reduce human suffering and help humanity as his duty? What I have done...")

My eyes closed. My heart was whipped.

It was Hauptmann's German drama "The Sunken Bell," which tells how the protagonist Heinrich is fascinated by Rautendelein and forgets his duties as a father and husband, and the pastor's advice to him is the same as the words my friend advised me three days ago. However, the protagonist of "The Sunken Bell" did not think of his wife and sons who lived off his tears until his death. What about me?

(What about me? What method do I use to get rid of these ah, these shackles of vanity and material enjoyment, which dominate me?

I lowered, lowered my slicked-back head. Something like a steel arrow seemed to have pierced right through my chest, causing a slight pain.

Opening "Dancing Girl"

Sighing frequently, sighing repeatedly. The dancing girl who runs the business is too unfeeling. Remembering meeting for the first time in the dancing hall. Falling in love at first sight. Remembering the intimate words whispered by the pillow. I thought it was a thousand-mile marriage led by a single thread. Who knew that the words were still ringing in my ears when the heart had already changed. Abandoning all previous affection in one stroke. Wishing I could cut you into two pieces. Cutting the threads of love to avoid hurting the spirit. I hate that you willingly betrayed the promises made before the flowers. What about living together in the same bed and dying together in the same grave? What about wishing to be birds flying wing to wing in heaven? What about wishing to be rooted trees growing inseparably on earth? Fortunately, my heart carefully awakened to the situation. Recognizing your false affection, false righteousness, and false diligence. I have spent countless money on you. I have been slighted several times. I have often quarreled with my wife because of you. Abandoning the love of a married couple. I have wasted time and lost my job for you, enduring much suffering. Friends and relatives have severed contact, not coming to my door. Now you are you and I am me. Beating the mandarin ducks, separating them in two places. I regret not listening to my wife's good advice. I regret not listening to my relatives' and friends' admonishments. It would be better to retreat while the tide is high and seek a way to make a living. A prodigal son can turn over a new leaf. I advise everyone to be careful when falling in love in the dancing hall.
