Shen Bao Local Supplement Movie Special Issue

Claudette Colbert's Correspondence with a Peculiar Fan (Part Two)

— Ti Yun

Several days passed, and the fan sent another letter, with nothing but the salutation and closing, and a small dot in the middle.

Claudette received the letter and couldn't help but laugh. The letters were getting simpler and simpler, so simple as to be just a dot. Then she had another whimsical idea: to write him a letter with nothing at all, not even a dot. So she wrote a letter, with only the salutation and closing, and a blank space in the middle, adding a line of small print below: "You think you're so clever, please fill it in yourself!" Sure enough, a thick reply arrived a few days later. In the fan's letter, he wrote, "As you commanded, I have filled in the blank space in your letter, but I wonder if you dare send it?"

Claudette Colbert laughed heartily upon hearing this, saying, "Look at the letter he wrote for me, how daring!" As she spoke, she handed the letter that Mr. Daniel Burke had written for her to the journalist. He took it and read it, and it said, "Dear Mr. Burke, I have read many of your letters, and I feel that you are not an unpleasant person. Why don't you come to Los Angeles for a visit? We can have a great time together. And using our correspondence as a benchmark, I believe we will talk endlessly after we meet. Come on. My heart is jumping for joy for you, and waiting for your glorious arrival!" At the end, he even signed it for her: "Your beloved, Claudette Colbert."

Since receiving that letter, Claudette Colbert knew that this joke had gone too far. How should she deal with it? If she really sent that letter, and the fan really ran to Hollywood to see her, wouldn't that make it even more difficult for her? But if she didn't send the letter, it would seem that she was a half-wit and lacked a sense of humor.

She was really hesitant. She put the letter in her wallet, took it from home to the studio, and from the studio to home. For a week, the letter was not sent. One day, she suddenly shouted her own name: "Claudette Colbert, you are really a fool!" She made up her mind and sent the letter. But she added a line at the end of the letter: "I dare to send the letter, but don't you dare to come!"

Three weeks after the letter was sent, one day Claudette was at the studio when a studio messenger handed her a letter. She took a look, and it was from the fan. She was having lunch in the dressing room at the time. She immediately opened the letter and read it. It said, "Dear Miss Colbert: I am very sorry for not being able to join you for lunch. The staff at the studio don't seem to believe me: where would a Mr. Daniel Burke come from, travelling all the way from Oklahoma to see you? Therefore, I left this letter, please have dinner with me at the Ambassador Hotel tonight." It was signed: "Your daring Daniel."

Claudette felt as if she had been electrocuted, and couldn't move. This guy really came! What to do? She didn't know what kind of person he was. Was he old? Young? She asked the studio messenger if he had seen the person. He shook his head and said no. Claudette then asked a friend to come and told him all about her predicament, asking him to go to the hotel first to take a look.

The friend returned after a while. He smiled and said, "Mr. Burke is a handsome man, the likes of which I have never seen before. He is over six feet tall and very burly. His skin is slightly dark. He is about thirty years old." Claudette's heart fluttered, and she couldn't wait to rush over and kiss him, but out of consideration, she wrote a letter, thanking him for the invitation, and inviting him to her home on a Friday evening for a chat.

Friday arrived. Half past seven arrived. Then Mr. Daniel Burke arrived. Claudette was combing her hair when her butler brought in a card, saying that Mr. Burke had arrived. Claudette said, "Please ask him to wait, I'll be down in a moment." The butler hesitated for a moment, then stammered, "Mr. Burke is a woman." Claudette was baffled. When she went down to see for herself, there was only an old lady in the drawing-room. She took a step forward when she saw Claudette and shook her hand. Her hair was snow white. Apart from a few small wrinkles, her skin was as red and tender as a child's. Her eyes deserved the elegant title of "clear, sparkling eyes," they were truly lively and lovely. She opened her mouth and said, "Let me introduce myself. I am Mrs. Lucy Pembroke, and I am the one who has been corresponding with you. Daniel Burke is just my pen name..."

Claudette rushed out again at this point in the story. After a while, she brought a large photograph. She said, "Look. This is Mr. Burke, the most interesting person. Whenever I encounter disappointment, I just need to see her photo, and all my anger disappears!" (The End)

Film Review

Review of "The Great Secret"

— Ling He

British Agent 丨 Grand Theater

Since the resumption of diplomatic relations between China and Russia, we have had the opportunity to appreciate many Soviet films. Since the restoration of normal relations between the United States and Russia, we have also had the opportunity to see American producers adapting Soviet revolutionary stories into films.

The Soviet Union is no longer regarded as a monster, and it recently joined the League of Nations, presiding over the important situation in Geneva. Therefore, the production of such works is not without commercial security, as the people of the world are paying attention to this new country. Thus, R.H. Bruce Lockhart's original work was portrayed on the Hollywood set.

Yes, this somewhat depicts the so-called revolution after the collapse of the Kerensky government, and how, under the Lenin-led regime, it made a separate peace with Germany and how it countered the intervention of European and American countries in the revolution. However, under the representation of American filmmakers, it cannot but be distorted, with many subjective fabrications deviating from the true historical record. Obviously, the playwright emphasized the opposition to the Soviet government's separate armistice, believing that it damaged the Allied front, and intentionally ignored the ardent desire for peace of the general public under the line of hunger and death at that time. (These are fully portrayed in Pudovkin's "The End of St. Petersburg" or other Soviet films.) Similarly, the essence of intervention in the revolution is also concealed under the pretext of opposing peace talks, with very little positive representation, although there is also an exposure of the international intervention conspiracy at the dance party. More importantly, the romance between the revolutionary female detective and the British diplomatic representative is exaggerated with great interest. In the entire film, the so-called entanglement of revolution and love occupies a very important part. In the end, the aristocratic revolutionary woman follows her lover back to the so-called beautiful and gentle England. Love triumphs over revolution, and this ending reveals the vulgarity of the playwright's ideas.

In any case, this is always a Soviet revolutionary story as understood by American filmmakers. If we compare the impressions we get from Soviet films with this, we can clearly see that under the same subject matter, there are completely different styles. Since the playwright's ideas are as described above, we will further explore the contrast in presentation techniques.

In Soviet films, what can usually be seen is the resolute, determined, brave, and straightforward national character, which Soviet writers express with a heavy atmosphere and relaxed tones. However, what is presented in "The Great Secret" is a completely American sentiment. On the one hand, the demeanor of the defense gentlemen, such as the protagonist Stan, is like that of an American young master officer, not to mention, but on the revolutionary woman, she is also not a Russian-flavored woman. In short, the inherent Russian life, habits, and emotions are not grasped in this. What we feel is always an American writer's representation of Russian thoughts, landscapes, and characters, without giving us a real and profound Russian flavor. What is gratifying is that for several leading figures of the time, such as Lenin, Stalin, and Kerensky, the actors' makeup is similar to what we see in the photos, especially Lenin's demeanor. In a novel translated by Ye Lingfeng, we once read such a description. This kind of aftertaste can make people feel interested. Beyond that, there is nothing else that needs to be mentioned.

"Lake and Mountain Song and Dance" 丨 Nanjing MGM 1935 Latest Song and Dance Hilarious Art Supreme Creation New Star Song and Dance Genius Maxi Tauffer Regan

"Resistance" Opens Today

"Resistance" is a film depicting the Great War in Europe. In addition to giving us the same thrilling stimulation as the several great war films seen before, this film skillfully contains extremely profound meaning and extremely interesting plot in the realistic depiction of war. Therefore, this film cannot be compared with other war films.

In terms of meaning, "Resistance" focuses on suggesting how people should prepare for national defense to cope with possible foreign troubles. At a time when the great powers are actively preparing for the Second World War, especially under the current situation in China today, this kind of film, which is intended to remind us and stimulate our nationalism, has its special status and the value of the times and cannot be ignored by us.

In terms of the plot, this film begins with how the German army sniped at the British and French Allied forces when everything was calm. Then it tells how the British and French Allied forces trained gunmen to deal with the German snipers. Finally, it ends with the ending of two Russian gunmen in the Allied forces. The evolution of the story is fascinating at every turn. It is also a characteristic of war films.

The film has Chinese and English subtitles, which can be said to be a unique feature of foreign films. It is said that the film will open today at the Carlton.

Yi Hua Presents Telephone Directory

Yi Hua Company has recently printed a pocket-sized telephone directory. The front is a telephone form, which can be filled with the telephone numbers of relatives and friends. The back is printed with a personal photo of Li Minghui, the heroine of the two new Yi Hua films "The Night Before the Wedding" and "Elegy of Life," which will soon be released at the Jincheng Grand Theater. Three-color fine printing, clear copper pictures, beautiful style, small and exquisite, easy to store in the wallet. It is now specially distributed to people from all walks of life. Those who ask for it in person will not be charged a penny. Those who ask for it by mail will be charged one cent for postage in this city and two cents for postage in other cities, and it will be sent immediately without delay. Those who ask for it in person can come to the business department of Yi Hua Company on the upper floor of the Baxianqiao Golden Theater or the general affairs department of Yi Hua Company on Kang Nao Road. However, those who ask for it by mail are limited to asking for it from the general affairs department of Yi Hua Company. The print run is not large, so ask for it as soon as possible.

Movie Novel

Forsaking All Others (7)

— Su Yin

After Connie appeared suddenly, Geoffrey also appeared suddenly. Geoffrey knew that Connie had a plan to trap Mary, so he was constantly on guard and followed Connie. But neither Connie nor Mary knew this. By the time Mary found out, she was already sitting in the car with Geoffrey. Connie's plan also failed to materialize.

But Mary still loved Dillon after all. Since their reunion after a long absence, the flame of love in her heart suddenly sprouted again. She thought it wouldn't hurt to meet occasionally, talk occasionally, and have a rare Sunday drive to the countryside together. She liked to see his smile, because he was a handsome man after all, and she had already promised her heart to him. Geoffrey later found out and had tried to persuade her bitterly, but she took his words as water off a duck's back, and it had no effect at all. One day, when she was in a hurry, she said, "Am I a shameless person, a lawbreaker, who can't meet a man?" Geoffrey also said, "Dillon is different! He once left you standing alone in front of the altar to get married. Besides, you already love him deeply, and you will disregard everything. You are hurting yourself." Mary said, "Alright, alright. I'm hurting myself! You don't have to worry about me, and you don't have to build any monuments to chastity." Sure enough, Geoffrey stopped interfering from then on.

One day, she and Dillon drove to the countryside to play again. They drove endlessly, wanting to go to Paula's house. Mary said, "That's an empty house in the countryside." Dillon said, "It won't be empty when we get there." Mary looked at Dillon's face, wanting to know what he meant. Dillon smiled and replied, "I love you." and lowered his head to kiss her. Mary's heart couldn't help but flutter, and she hooked her arms around Dillon's neck. In that instant, something went wrong. The car fell into a ditch by the road!

They had no choice but to leave the car and walk on the dirt road. They walked countless miles, walking until they were covered in sweat, with no romance to speak of. Finally, they came to a gas station, but there was no one there to repair cars. Fortunately, there was a young man there who drove them for a while, taking them to the house closest to Paula's, asking them to go there first to get the key to the empty house. They took the key, and then set off on foot again. But the heavens were not beautiful, and a heavy rain started. Therefore, by the time they reached their destination, they were both soaked to the skin.

They entered the house and rummaged around for old clothes. But they only found some of Paula's shirts, so Dillon could only take off his own clothes and put on women's shirts. Afternoon turned into dusk. Dusk turned into night. At first, when they were at the gas station, Mary had asked Dillon to make a phone call and ask his waiter Johnson to bring the car to pick them up. But Dillon deliberately didn't make the call. Now, Dillon himself regretted it. Because there was nothing to eat in this empty house. They found a can of sardines, but after the can was opened, it accidentally fell to the ground and was eaten by the cat.

With nothing to think about and nothing to do, they could only light a kerosene lamp and light a fire in the fireplace to keep warm. After a while, Dillon suddenly thought of a wonderful way to keep warm. He suddenly put his arms around Mary and kissed her, saying, "I love you so much..." Mary pushed him away and pointed to something on the piano and said, "Look. What is that?" Dillon took a look and couldn't help but feel angry. It turned out to be a cat, the cat that had just eaten the sardines, sitting obediently on the piano and looking at them. Dillon grabbed a pillow and shouted, "Get out of here!" and threw it over. Mary quickly called out to stop him, but it was too late. Another disaster. (To be continued)
